# Apollo — Learning-by-Teaching Subsystem

Apollo inverts tutoring: the student explains a concept, Apollo plays a learner that knows
nothing, and at "I'm done teaching" the explanation is graded by diffing the student's
knowledge graph (KG) against an authored reference graph. State is split across two stores:
Postgres (Supabase) owns sessions/messages/attempts/progress; Neo4j owns the per-attempt KG
subgraph. The current architecture is "diff-at-Done v1" (spec: workspace
`docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-09-apollo-diff-at-done-design.md`, outside this repo):
the per-turn loop is just **nodify + dumb reply**; the output filter and SymPy solver were
unwired (code still present). Done grading has two default-OFF served evidence sources:
the legacy graph-node semantic diff, and the transcript-first adjudicator selected by
`APOLLO_TRANSCRIPT_GRADER`. The latter makes one strict structured-output call over the
full both-role dialogue and grades knowledge demonstrated by the student's own words:
an item may be explicitly `stated`, correctly `used`, clearly `implied`, or `absent`.
**The transcript LLM adjudicator is the grader of record (2026-07-11)**: it assigns each
rubric item a continuous credit in `[0, 1]` and that number flows through UNCHANGED all the
way to the served topic score — no deterministic post-processing second-guesses it. The
`stated`/`used`/`implied`/`absent` basis is reported provenance (prompt guidance and a
logging field on the verdict) — no code branches on it; the former `implied` → 0.7 cap and
`absent` → forced-zero overrides are gone. Every positive credit still asks the model to
quote a supporting span from a student message, but span validation
(`transcript_coverage.py::validate_span`) is diagnostic logging only — it never zeroes or
downgrades credit in the serving lane (it remains the gate for the offline
`campaign/transcript_replay.py` fixture-replay harness). The adjudicator then emits the
frozen legacy coverage dict (`per_step`/`procedure_scores`) consumed by rubric, topic score,
diagnostic, XP, and artifacts; `per_step`'s binary "covered" still needs `credit >= 0.5` (kept
for parity with the graph lane's own scored threshold) but no longer decides the credit
number itself. **Topic credit equals the adjudicator's per-node credit**: `topic_score.py::_credit_for_node`
reads `procedure_scores[node_id]` whenever the node is present there — a `per_step` "covered"
status no longer promotes credit to a hard `1.0`; that promotion only remains as the fallback
for a node absent from `procedure_scores` entirely. This applies to BOTH grading lanes' topic
projection (the shadow graph-lane coverage dict shares the same `per_step`/`procedure_scores`
shape, so its topic score is affected identically). The response always includes
`grading_provenance`, naming the served
evidence source and exposing pre-dock score, per-topic docks, and graph-lane abstention.
Misconception arithmetic is localized: attached findings subtract only inside their
topic contribution; unattached findings retain the global `SEVERITY_CLAMP` cap.

The default-off `APOLLO_SMART_QUESTIONS_ENABLED` path replaces the per-turn dumb reply
with three reference-driven stages: `smart_questions.evaluator` judges the cumulative
student-only transcript against **every** authored reference node; the pure planner chooses
one prerequisite-ready `partial`/`missing`/`misconceived` node that has never been asked;
and the answer-blind writer asks one short question without receiving the student KG. A
private-target phrase guard falls back to a generic probe if wording leaks an answer. The
`apollo_reference_question_opportunities` ledger enforces one opportunity per
`(attempt_id, reference_node_id)`. After the response, that opportunity is terminal even
when coverage remains insufficient. When all nodes are covered or every remaining gap has
already had its opportunity, chat persists a closing turn and invokes the existing Done
handler; its embedded result uses the existing UI auto-report seam. Flag OFF leaves the
legacy chat and clarification paths unchanged.

**GEN-0 selector/provenance hardening (2026-07-12).** The shared
`overseer.problem_selector.list_problems_for_concept` chokepoint validates Tier-2
payloads one row at a time. A malformed row emits the structured warning
`apollo_problem_selector_invalid_payload_skipped` with concept, tier, row id, and a
bounded validation summary, then is skipped; valid siblings remain selectable by both
standard and personalized selection. An entirely malformed pool therefore reaches the
existing `PoolExhaustedError` path. At the persistence boundary, `ConceptProblem`
enforces the provenance invariant that `provenance.source="generated"` may carry only
`solution_source="generated"` (or remain unset while generation is pending), never the
teacher-grounded `extracted` or `authored` labels. The validation is assignment-order
independent, so it covers insert-time stamping and later promotion updates.

**GEN-2 problem-generation authoring stage (2026-07-12).**
`apollo/provisioning/problem_generation/` provides the teacher-initiated
“generate N more problems like these” library behind the per-call,
default-OFF `APOLLO_PROBLEM_GENERATION` flag. It cycles valid Tier-2 seed
problems through subject-agnostic variation operators, generates a statement,
reuses `find_or_generate` for a reference DAG, rejects normalized duplicates,
runs a pure SymPy round-trip verifier, and rejects answer leaks before writing
explicit Tier-1 `solution_source="generated"` rows. Self-refuting variants are
dropped; verified, unresolved, and inapplicable verdicts are retained in
provenance. Inapplicable prose variants that pass the leak guard also receive a
fail-open, advisory claim-decomposition rubric whose validation ceiling is
explicitly `faithfulness_only`. Every written row is held for teacher review
through the existing
`provenance.authored_review.ocr_draft` handoff; GEN-2 never promotes content or
changes the approve → lint → promote chain. Per-run token ceilings are exposed
for the caller's `MeteredChat`, and a mid-run budget breach returns already
written rows as a partial result. GEN-4 exposes that library through the
teacher-gated `/apollo/problem-generation` API: POSTing a concept batch creates
an `apollo_generation_runs` row and processes it in an in-process background
task, the run list/detail endpoints expose bounded status, cost, and generated
problem review projections, a seeds endpoint lists the concept's teachable
(tier-2, non-quarantined) problems for the UI's seed picker (not flag-gated,
like the run reads), and the generated-problem approve endpoint reuses
the authored-set approve core to mint, lint, and promote a selected held draft.
`GenerationRun` links the course and concept to the optional `IngestRun` that
owns LLM call/token/cost aggregates; generation remains default-OFF while run
reads and approval of already-generated content remain available.

## Module map and file landmarks

| Subpackage | Key files | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `apollo/` (root) | `api.py`, `auth_deps.py`, `errors.py`, `conftest.py` | FastAPI router (prefix `/apollo`), auth dependency functions, per-error exception handlers, process-singleton Neo4j client (`get_neo4j_client`/`close_neo4j_client`). `errors.py`: one named exception per failure mode, NO FALLBACK policy. **WU-4C1** registers five more Done shadow-chain error handlers in `register_exception_handlers`: `ResolutionUnavailableError`→503 `resolution_unavailable` (`stage`,`last_error`), `TranscriptAuditUnavailableError`→503 `transcript_audit_unavailable` (`stage`,`last_error`), `ResolutionInvalidOutputError`→500 `resolution_invalid_output` (`returned_key`,`allowed_key_count` — bounded, NOT the full key list), `StudentGraphInvalidError`→422 `student_graph_invalid` (`reasons`), `ReferenceGraphInvalidError`→409 `reference_graph_invalid` (`reasons`); the two 503s carry a non-fatal "your grade is saved; grading is computing in the background" message (the SHADOW failure never voids the student grade). The two validator errors import from `apollo.graph_compare.validator`, the other three from `apollo.errors`. `CanonProjectionError` is deliberately NOT in the five (it surfaces as a generic 500 in v1 SHADOW — a registered handler is a follow-up). **WU-5B3a-0** adds `LearnerUpdateUnreconstructableError(*, attempt_id, reason)` (mirrors `RetentionError`) + the closed `LEARNER_UPDATE_UNRECONSTRUCTABLE_REASONS = (diagnostic_report_missing, rubric_missing, graded_at_missing)` tuple — the terminal dead-letter `build_rerun_inputs`'s pre-flight raises when re-run inputs are unreconstructable from durable state; the WU-5B3a-1 janitor catches it and marks the row `learner_update_failed_permanently` (no backoff, no LLM). NOT HTTP-registered (offline janitor path; on the live Done path the inputs are always reconstructable, so it never fires there). `conftest.py`: live Neo4j fixture (skips if `NEO4J_URI` unset; test attempt_ids must be NEGATIVE — cleanup deletes `attempt_id < 0`). **Task B3** adds `GET /teacher/classroom/{search_space_id}/heatmap` and `GET /teacher/classroom/{search_space_id}/struggles` (the latter takes an optional `window_days` query param, default `apollo.projections.classroom.DEFAULT_WINDOW_DAYS=14`) — both gated by `require_course_teacher` (NOT `require_course_member`: these expose every student's per-entity mastery state, so auto-enrolling students must never satisfy the check), thin wrappers over `apollo.projections.classroom.mastery_heatmap`/`struggle_signals`. |
| `apollo/handlers/` | `browse.py`, `chat.py`, `done.py`, `done_grading.py`, `done_inputs.py`, `done_turn_order.py`, `learner_update.py`, `learner_janitor.py`, `intent.py`, `lifecycle.py`, `negotiate.py`, `next.py`, `restart_problem.py`, `progress.py`, `history.py`, `olm_invite.py` | One module per endpoint group. `browse.py` = read-only student browse (`handle_list_problems`: one concept's tier-2 non-quarantined pool, `attempted`-flagged from the caller's own `ProblemAttempt` rows, course-scope-checked via `list_course_concepts` → 409; student-safety invariant — only `{id, difficulty, problem_text, attempted}`, never `reference_solution`/`given_values`/`target_unknown`). `chat.py` = teaching turn + intent state machine; `done.py` = freeze → OLD grade/XP/retention (student-facing, UNCHANGED) → **shadow graph-simulation chain behind `APOLLO_GRAPH_SIM_SHADOW_ENABLED`** (default OFF in prod, ON in test). When the flag is OFF, `handle_done`'s return is byte-identical to today and `run_graph_simulation` is never called; when ON, the chain runs AFTER the OLD grade/XP are durable and persists a comparison run + findings ALONGSIDE the unchanged student grade. The student-facing dict is built from OLD-path values ONLY (the shadow result is NEVER merged in). The shadow chain reads the RAW `ConceptProblem.payload` (the parsed `Problem` schema DROPS `declared_paths`/`symbolic_mappings`/per-step `entity_key`, which the chain needs) via `_find_problem_payload` — RELOCATED to `done_inputs.py` as of WU-5B3a-0 (re-exported from `done.py`), now sourced through `build_rerun_inputs` (see below). **`done_grading.py`** (WU-4C1) holds `ShadowGradeResult` (frozen WU-4C2/WU-5A handoff: `run_id`/`grade`/`audited`/`normalization_confidence`/`reference_graph_hash`/`opposes_map`/`turn_order`) + `run_graph_simulation(db, neo, *, attempt, sess, student_graph, problem_payload)` — the §6.4 chain `resolve → RESOLVES_TO → canonicalize → grade → audit → persist run+findings` (every callee DONE/frozen, only CALLED, no new grading algorithm); at Step 5 it FIRST loads the attempt's confirmed clarifications via `load_confirmed_resolutions(db, attempt_id)` and threads them into `resolve_attempt(confirmed_resolutions=...)` as AUTHORITATIVE mappings (the @0.90 clarification method — the G2 payoff that lets a student-confirmed idea clear the abstention floor before the fuzzy/LLM tiers fire); it owns the run-txn `db.commit()` after `persist_comparison_run` (which flushes only). NO-FALLBACK / staged-txn: a step-5+ infra failure (`ResolutionUnavailableError`/`ResolutionInvalidOutputError`/`TranscriptAuditUnavailableError`/unexpected `Exception` incl. `CanonProjectionError`) sets `attempt.learner_update_pending=True`, commits that flag, and RE-RAISES the named error (NEVER voids the already-committed student grade); `StudentGraphInvalidError` (422) / `ReferenceGraphInvalidError` (409) raise BEFORE any cross-store write and do NOT set `learner_update_pending`. It does NOT call `convert_findings_to_events` and does NOT write `apollo_mastery_events`/`apollo_learner_state` (WU-5A). **WU-4C2** EXTENDS `ShadowGradeResult` with three additive REQUIRED fields — `graph_sim_rubric` (the graph-sim candidate grade from `build_graph_sim_rubric`), `calibration` (the §6.7 `CalibrationMetrics` shadow-vs-OLD), `diagnostic` (the §6.8 `ConstrainedDiagnostic`) — and `run_graph_simulation` gains a keyword-only `old_rubric: dict` arg (the OLD student-facing rubric, threaded from `done.py`, for calibration); these three are computed INSIDE the existing `try:` AFTER the run-txn commit (pure rubric/calibration + soft-failing-injected diagnostic), `_LOG.info("graph_sim_calibration", ...)` records letter_agreement/overall_score_delta/divergent, and any defensive failure still follows the WU-4C1 NO-FALLBACK fork (no new except). `done.py` gains the DORMANT `_GRAPH_SIM_LIVE_FLAG = "APOLLO_GRAPH_SIM_LIVE_ENABLED"` (+ `_graph_sim_live_enabled()`, default OFF EVERYWHERE incl. test): it gates only PROMOTION of the shadow `graph_sim_rubric`/`diagnostic.narrative` to the student-facing `rubric`/`diagnostic_narrative` keys — when OFF (the only build state) the return is byte-identical to WU-4C1; when ON (built + unit-tested, never enabled) those two keys are REPLACED while coverage/progress/XP stay OLD-path. Promotion is reached only after a successful shadow chain (a raised shadow never promotes — the OLD grade stands). **`done_turn_order.py`** (WU-4C1) = `build_turn_order(db, neo, *, attempt_id, student_graph) -> dict[node_id,int]`: maps each KG node to a monotone turn position from the node's Neo4j `created_at` (via `KGStore.read_node_created_at`, since `read_graph` strips it) joined to the nearest at-or-before `apollo_messages.turn_index`, falling back to the bare ascending ordinal when no message rows exist; a node with no `created_at` is an ABSENT key (events.py tolerates via `_SENTINEL_TURN`). `intent.py` = cheap-LLM intent classifier + confirmation gate; `history.py` = bounded history (12-turn raw window + rolling LLM summary); `negotiate.py` = Negotiable-OLM moves (challenge/paraphrase/skip/trace); `olm_invite.py` = low-confidence clarification invite (env-flagged, currently not wired into the v1 chat turn). **WU-5A2** adds `learner_update.py` (`run_learner_update(db, *, sess, attempt, shadow, done_ts, parser_confidence) -> LearnerUpdateResult | None`) — the Layer-3 transaction OWNER + NO-FALLBACK fork: it re-derives the `{spec.canonical_key: spec.key}` map via `load_entity_specs(db, search_space_id=sess.search_space_id, concept_id=sess.concept_id)`, calls the flush-only `persist_learner_update`, then owns the SINGLE `db.commit()` (the all-or-nothing boundary). On ANY exception inside the txn it rolls back the Layer-3 work, sets `attempt.learner_update_pending = True`, commits THAT flag in a separate txn, and RE-RAISES the original error (the OLD grade/XP + shadow run are already durable, so the grade is NEVER voided — mirrors `done_grading._set_pending_and_commit`). `done.py` gains the DORMANT `_GRAPH_SIM_LAYER3_FLAG = "APOLLO_GRAPH_SIM_LAYER3_ENABLED"` (+ `_graph_sim_layer3_enabled()`, default OFF EVERYWHERE incl. test): inside the `if _graph_sim_shadow_enabled():` block, AFTER the WU-4C2 LIVE-promotion check, `if shadow is not None and _graph_sim_layer3_enabled():` it computes `parser_confidence = min_parser_confidence_of(student_graph.nodes)` and awaits `run_learner_update`. `done.py` also captures ONE `done_ts = datetime.now(UTC)` at the stamp site and threads it into BOTH `stamp_graded_at(ts=done_ts)` (Neo4j `graded_at`) and `run_learner_update(done_ts=done_ts)` (Postgres `last_evidence_at`/`updated_at`) so the two stores stamp the IDENTICAL freeze instant. When the Layer-3 flag is OFF (the only build state) the gated call NEVER fires and `handle_done`'s return + DB side-effects are byte-identical to WU-4C2 (`test_done_shadow_route_postgres.py` me==0/ls==0 stays green). No migration (026 already shipped the tables/CHECKs/UNIQUE/`learner_update_pending`). **WU-5B1 adds `_LEARNER_DECAY_FLAG = "APOLLO_LEARNER_DECAY_ENABLED"` (+ `_learner_decay_enabled()`, default OFF EVERYWHERE — mirrors `done.py`'s flag-helper shape) to `learner_update.py`:** when ON, `run_learner_update` builds a `prior_transform` CLOSURE binding `decay_toward_prior(belief, COLD_START_PRIOR, dt_days)` (a `None` dt → identity, defensive symmetry with the `decay_weight` clamp) and threads it into `persist_learner_update(prior_transform=…)`; when OFF it passes `None` (byte-identical to WU-5A2). `run_learner_update`'s public signature is UNCHANGED (the flag is read INTERNALLY, so the `done.py` call site stays byte-identical and `done.py` is untouched). No migration (`dt_days_since_last` already populated by WU-5A2). **WU-5B2 adds `_LEARNER_NEGOTIATION_FLAG = "APOLLO_LEARNER_NEGOTIATION_ENABLED"` (+ `_learner_negotiation_enabled()`, default OFF EVERYWHERE — mirrors `_learner_decay_enabled`) to `learner_update.py`:** when ON, `run_learner_update` reads this attempt's student moves ONCE via `load_student_moves(db, attempt_id=…)` (actor='student', latest-wins) and builds two per-entity CLOSURES over the in-memory `moves` dict — `negotiation_move_for_entity` (the representative move, persisted on each event row) and `likelihood_multiplier_for_entity` (which applies the RATIFIED suppression: a misconception entity → `NO_OP_LIKELIHOOD` identity, else `negotiation_multiplier(entity_negotiation_move(...))`) — and threads BOTH into `persist_learner_update(likelihood_multiplier_for_entity=…, negotiation_move_for_entity=…)`; when OFF both stay `None` (identity-default → byte-identical to WU-5B1). `run_learner_update`'s public signature is UNCHANGED (flag read INTERNALLY; `done.py` untouched). No migration (`negotiation_move` + `apollo_kg_negotiations` already exist). The §3 multiplier now CONSUMES `apollo_kg_negotiations` at the fold (read-only, student-actor, latest-wins) — distinct from `negotiate.py`'s OLM write path and the Done-gate's lossy read. **WU-5B3a-0** adds `done_inputs.py` (`build_rerun_inputs(db, neo, *, attempt, sess) -> RerunInputs`) — the single source of truth for re-assembling the `run_graph_simulation` inputs, keyed on **`attempt.problem_id`** (NEVER `sess.current_problem_id` — the durable per-attempt key, so the WU-5B3a janitor reconstructs the OLD problem even after `next.py` advanced the session), sourcing `old_rubric` from `attempt.diagnostic_report['rubric']` and the `done_ts` from Neo4j `graded_at`; it raises `LearnerUpdateUnreconstructableError` (terminal dead-letter, no LLM) when `diagnostic_report` is None / lacks `rubric`/`overall` or the Neo4j subgraph has no `graded_at`. The frozen `RerunInputs` carries `problem_payload`/`old_rubric`/`student_graph`/`parser_confidence`/`graded_at_iso` (the raw ISO string — the janitor parses it tz-aware). `_find_problem_payload` is RELOCATED from `done.py` into `done_inputs.py` (re-exported from `done.py` — SAME object, no duplicate def); `done.py`'s shadow chain now sources `problem_payload` through `build_rerun_inputs` (behavior-preserving — `student_graph`/`old_rubric` stay the LIVE values, the route tests stay green). The five new columns + index are migration-028 DDL only — nothing reads/writes them in this unit (the WU-5B3a-1 drain state machine consumes them). **WU-5B3a-1** adds `learner_janitor.py` (`drain_pending_attempts(neo, *, limit=1, max_attempts=MAX_ATTEMPTS, user_id=None) -> DrainResult`) — the retry-janitor DRAIN state machine that CONSUMES the migration-028 columns. It claims one due `learner_update_pending` (not-dead) attempt with `FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED` + a `CLAIM_LEASE_S` work-lease (one short claim-txn that bumps `learner_update_attempts` and COMMITs immediately, mirroring `teacher_weekly._claim_upload_job_async`), re-runs the frozen `build_rerun_inputs` → `run_graph_simulation` → (LAYER3-gated) `run_learner_update` in a SEPARATE work session, then in a THIRD record-txn (re-SELECT by id, mirroring `_handle_job_failure_async`) clears `learner_update_pending` on success / sets `learner_update_failed_permanently` on `LearnerUpdateUnreconstructableError` (terminal, no backoff/LLM — a vanished-problem `NoResultFound` is also classified terminal) / backs off `learner_update_next_attempt_at` by the pinned schedule (300/1200/3600 ±10% jitter) on transient failure, dead-lettering at `attempts >= MAX_ATTEMPTS=3`. The belief write is interlocked on `_graph_sim_layer3_enabled()` (the back-door guard): LAYER3 OFF → `run_graph_simulation` re-runs (supersede-idempotent) but the belief write is DEFERRED (row left pending, the at-claim bump is UNDONE so the deferral does not consume a retry; a DISTINCT `learner_janitor_layer3_deferred` warning is emitted so a "worker on, LAYER3 off, backlog never clears" misconfig is visible). The clear-flag lives in the janitor record-txn (NOT in frozen `run_learner_update`) to preserve the WU-5A2 byte-identity guardrail; a crash between the fold-commit and the clear can re-increment `evidence_count` by at most +1/entity (belief stays correct — accepted bound). Two clocks, both correct: the claim/backoff schedule uses wall-clock `now()` (SQL), while the belief Δt anchor uses the FROZEN Neo4j `graded_at` (`graded_at_iso` parsed tz-aware, NEVER `now()`); a naive (offset-less) `graded_at` parse defensively dead-letters (`graded_at_missing`). Named constants `MAX_ATTEMPTS`/`BASE_DELAY_S`/`BACKOFF_FACTOR`/`MAX_DELAY_S`/`JITTER`/`CLAIM_LEASE_S` are env-overridable (`APOLLO_JANITOR_*`). It opens its OWN per-phase `get_async_session()` (short-txn discipline — it takes NO `db` arg). NO worker loop / Procfile / opportunistic backstop here (WU-5B3b). The three test harnesses are split by shape so the right `neo4j_client` resolves: **H1** (`apollo/handlers/tests/test_learner_janitor.py`, savepoint `db_session`, Neo4j+LLM stubbed) drives drain/accounting/dead-letter/backoff/LAYER3-defer/supersede-idempotency/connection-drop; **H2** (`tests/database/test_learner_janitor_contention.py`, two committed connections via a real pooled engine on the migrated DSN) is the load-bearing SKIP-LOCKED two-claimer + claim-lease + claim-visibility proof; **H3** (`tests/database/test_learner_janitor_full_drain.py`, Testcontainers `neo4j:5.25` `neo4j_client`, LLM stubbed) is the one real full drain reading the frozen graph from real Neo4j (asserting `LearnerState.last_evidence_at == stamped graded_at`, not `now()`). **Campaign-plan Task A3 adds `artifact_writer.py`** (`write_artifacts(db, *, attempt, sess, shadow, coverage, rubric, served, graph_failure, latency_ms) -> dict | None`) — the paired canonical-artifact writer called from `done.py` under the NEW `APOLLO_GRADING_ARTIFACT_ENABLED` flag (default OFF, orthogonal to `APOLLO_GRAPH_SIM_SHADOW_ENABLED`). It builds the LLM payload via `build_llm_artifact` ALWAYS and the graph payload via `build_graph_artifact` only when `shadow is not None`, assembles the clarification trace itself (`_load_clarification_trace`: one row per `apollo_clarifications` record for the attempt, `credit="granted"` for `confirmed`/`"denied"` for `refuted`/`vague`/`None` while still `asked_waiting`), then writes ONE `role="canonical"` `GradingArtifact` row for whichever grade `served` names (`"llm_fallback"` in this build — Task A4's `APOLLO_GRAPH_GRADER_LIVE` is the only flag that can pass `"graph"`) plus a `role="pair"` row for the OTHER grade when both were computed. Own failure domain: the WHOLE body runs inside one `try/except Exception` that logs `artifact_write_failed` and rolls back the session — SOFTER than the shadow chain's NO-FALLBACK contract, since a telemetry-write failure must never cost a student their already-committed grade. In `done.py`, `_artifact_t0 = time.monotonic()` is captured immediately before the OLD `compute_coverage` call so a persisted artifact's `grading_latency_ms` spans the WHOLE grading pipeline (OLD path + shadow chain, when it runs); `shadow` is declared `None` before the `if _graph_sim_shadow_enabled():` block so the single `write_artifacts` call site AFTER that block (still gated on `_grading_artifact_enabled()`) sees `None` when the shadow flag is off and the real result when it ran. **Campaign-plan Task A4 adds `_GRAPH_GRADER_LIVE_FLAG = "APOLLO_GRAPH_GRADER_LIVE"` (+ `_graph_grader_live_enabled()`, default OFF EVERYWHERE) to `done.py`** — the spec's actual live-promotion switch (§3/§5), OPERATIONALLY SUPERSEDING the older dormant `APOLLO_GRAPH_SIM_LIVE_ENABLED` (WU-4C2, left untouched, never both on in a real deployment). The `if _graph_sim_shadow_enabled():` body is now wrapped in `try/except Exception as e` gated on `live = _graph_grader_live_enabled()`: when `live` is `False` (SHADOW mode — how staging/prod run during calibration), the boundary forks on exception TYPE (**lane B1 / G3 fix, narrowed**): the CONTRACTUAL typed failure modes in `_SHADOW_PROPAGATE_ERRORS` — exactly the shadow-chain error types whose registered route handlers (`apollo/api.py::register_exception_handlers`) map to a NON-500 response: `ResolutionUnavailableError` (503), `TranscriptAuditUnavailableError` (503), `StudentGraphInvalidError` (422), `ReferenceGraphInvalidError` (409) — keep RE-RAISING exactly as pre-G3, preserving their pinned commit semantics (pending set + committed for the retryable 503s; no pending for the two pre-cross-store validator errors; load-bearing route tests: `tests/database/test_done_shadow_route_postgres.py`). Everything else — the UNEXPECTED class, including the G3 repro `KeyError('variable_mapping')`, `CanonProjectionError`, and `ResolutionInvalidOutputError` (whose handler maps to 500, exactly the "shadow bug 500s the live grade" class) — is ISOLATED, NOT re-raised (`_SHADOW_FAILURE_MARKER = "shadow_failure: "`): it is logged (`apollo_graph_shadow_failure`, with `attempt_id`+`session_id`), `shadow` is reset to `None`, `graph_failure = f"{_SHADOW_FAILURE_MARKER}{repr(e)}"[:500]` (a shadow-failure marker DISTINCT from the LIVE path's bare `repr(e)`, so paired analysis can grep it to tell "the shadow chain crashed so there is no `pair` row" apart from "the live grader crashed and fell back"), and `served_grade` stays `GRADER_USED_LLM_FALLBACK` — the OLD/LLM student-facing values are already computed above and are never touched, so the response is HTTP 200 byte-identical to a shadow-OFF Done-click and the student NEVER loses their already-committed grade to a shadow bug. The marker rides `abstention.graph_failure` on the canonical LLM `GradingArtifact` row (no new column, no migration). Pre-G3 the unexpected class re-raised as a raw 500 (a shadow `KeyError('variable_mapping')` at `done_grading` step 3 would 500 the Done request and kill the live grade); the shadow chain's OWN internal NO-FALLBACK bookkeeping (`learner_update_pending` set + committed on a cross-store failure) still runs BEFORE the error reaches the boundary — G3 only stops the unexpected exception from reaching the HTTP layer. Unit coverage: `apollo/handlers/tests/test_done_shadow_isolation.py` (early/mid/late crash byte-identity vs a shadow-off control, the four-type propagation contract, the propagate-list pin, LIVE-mode guards). When `live` is `True`, ANY exception anywhere in the block (including a WU-4C2/WU-5A2 dormant-flag failure, since those checks run inside the same `try:`) is logged (`apollo_graph_grader_live_failure`), `shadow` is reset to `None`, `graph_failure = repr(e)[:500]`, and `served_grade` stays `GRADER_USED_LLM_FALLBACK` — the OLD/LLM student-facing values are already computed above and are never touched, so the response is HTTP 200 with the OLD grade. On success, a NEW promotion check — independent of the dormant WU-4C2 block — fires: `if live and shadow is not None and not shadow.audited.abstained:` replaces `student_response["rubric"]`/`["diagnostic_narrative"]` with `shadow.graph_sim_rubric`/`shadow.diagnostic.narrative` and sets `served_grade = GRADER_USED_GRAPH` (spec step 2-3: abstained ⇒ the session-time clarification loop already ran, so Done-time falls straight to the LLM values without re-running anything; `shadow` — carrying the real `abstention_reasons` — is still forwarded to `write_artifacts` unchanged, so the paired graph artifact records them). The single `write_artifacts` call site now passes `served=served_grade, graph_failure=graph_failure` instead of the A3 build's hardcoded `served=GRADER_USED_LLM_FALLBACK, graph_failure=None`. **Task B1** — `write_artifacts` now returns the CANONICAL payload dict it just persisted (`None` on its own swallowed write failure); `done.py` calls `apollo.projections.scorecard.render_scorecard` on that return value and attaches the additive `student_response["scorecard"]` key only when non-`None`, so a failed artifact write means no scorecard rather than templating a payload that never reached disk. Flag OFF is the only build state and is proven byte-identical to the pre-A4 golden in `apollo/handlers/tests/test_done_graph_grader_live.py`. **Task B2** — `done.py` gains `_project_mastery(db, *, attempt_id)`, called right after a successful artifact write (`canonical_payload is not None`), still gated on `APOLLO_GRADING_ARTIFACT_ENABLED`: it re-SELECTs the just-committed `role="canonical"` `GradingArtifact` row (its `id`/`created_at` only exist post-commit) and calls `apollo.projections.mastery.update_mastery_from_artifact`, then owns its OWN commit — an own-failure-domain posture mirroring `write_artifacts` (ANY exception is logged `mastery_projection_failed` and swallowed, session rolled back, NEVER raised into the Done response). Guarded MUTUALLY EXCLUSIVE with the dormant WU-5A2 belief path: `if _graph_sim_layer3_enabled():` logs `mastery_projection_skipped_layer3_active` and skips the call instead — both write `apollo_mastery_events`/`apollo_learner_state` and must never both fire for the same attempt. |
| `apollo/` (root, worker) | `learner_janitor_worker.py`, `provision_worker.py` | **WU-5B3b** adds `learner_janitor_worker.py` — the dormant `apollo-janitor` Procfile process (`apollo-janitor: python -m apollo.learner_janitor_worker`). An async-native poll loop (`main()` builds ONE `Neo4jClient.from_env()`, installs SIGTERM/SIGINT handlers on the running loop, runs `_loop`, and ALWAYS `await neo.close()` in a `finally`; the whole process stays on a SINGLE `asyncio.run(main())` loop so `database.session`'s `id(loop)`-keyed engine registry resolves the SAME engine for every drain phase — never bridged through the sync `run_async` daemon). `_loop` is `while not stop_event.is_set(): await _run_one_iteration(...)`; `_run_one_iteration` reads the flag PER PASS (`_janitor_enabled()`, default OFF EVERYWHERE) and, when ON, calls the FROZEN `drain_pending_attempts(neo, limit=SWEEP_LIMIT=1, max_attempts=MAX_ATTEMPTS)` once and logs the returned `DrainResult` (`apollo_janitor_sweep` with the six counts), then `await asyncio.sleep(POLL_SECONDS=60)`; when OFF it skips the drain (`apollo_janitor_disabled`) and just sleeps so a flag flip is picked up next pass. The drain call is wrapped in `try/except Exception: _LOG.exception("apollo_janitor_sweep_failed")` (R3 — one bad sweep must not kill the worker; `KeyboardInterrupt`/`SystemExit` still propagate). It gates ONLY on the janitor flag — the LAYER3 belief-write interlock lives INSIDE the frozen drain (`_graph_sim_layer3_enabled`). SIGTERM/SIGINT register `stop_event.set` via `loop.add_signal_handler`, wrapped in `try/except (NotImplementedError, RuntimeError)` (Windows ProactorEventLoop / non-main-thread → `apollo_janitor_signal_handler_unsupported` WARNING, no crash); shutdown is COOPERATIVE BETWEEN drains (`stop_event` checked at the TOP of each pass — a set event exits AFTER the current iteration, never mid-row; a row killed between sweeps re-drains via the drain's claim-lease). It REUSES `MAX_ATTEMPTS`/`_int_env`/`drain_pending_attempts`/`DrainResult` by import from the FROZEN `handlers/learner_janitor.py` (single source of truth, no redefinition). Adds NO drain logic / SQL / migration — a thin process wrapper around WU-5B3a-1. The flag is `APOLLO_AUTOPROVISION_ENABLED` (default OFF EVERYWHERE; `_autoprovision_enabled()` read PER PASS) — when OFF NOTHING drains, so a teacher upload behaves byte-identically and no auto-provisioned content reaches a student without a human deploy step (the process also ships scaled to 0 replicas). When ON, each sweep runs the **lease-reaper FIRST** (`_reap_expired(get_async_session)`, §9 OPS-5: every `apollo_provisioning_jobs` row that is `state='running' AND lease_expires_at < now()` has its linked `apollo_ingest_runs.status` flipped to `'failed'` so a crashed mid-document run is NEVER left `'running'` wedging the partial-unique-index; the FROZEN claim re-claims the job itself on lease expiry) THEN `_drain_one` (claim 3B2f → build a `MeteredChat` bound to the claimed run row → `run_provisioning` → `complete_job` on a succeeded outcome else `fail_job`), logging ONE `apollo_provision_sweep` line per drained job (`run_id`/`status`/`n_promoted`/`n_rejected`/`llm_cost`). The reap+drain is wrapped in `try/except Exception: _LOG.exception("apollo_provision_sweep_failed")` (one bad sweep survives; `KeyboardInterrupt`/`SystemExit` propagate). `_int_env` / `SWEEP_LIMIT`/`POLL_SECONDS`/`LEASE_SECONDS` mirror the janitor's `_int_env`-read env knobs (`APOLLO_PROVISION_*`). | `apollo/knowledge_graph/` | `store.py`, `canon_projection.py`, `resolution_store.py` | `KGStore(db, neo)`: Neo4j CRUD (`write_nodes`/`write_edges`/`read_graph`/`walk_chain`/`delete_subgraph`/`stamp_graded_at`), Postgres-backed freeze/unfreeze, `summarize_for_apollo()` bullet summary, and the three OLM negotiation moves with Postgres audit logging. As of WU-2B, `write_edges` validates endpoint existence + EDGE_ALLOWED_PAIRS BEFORE issuing any CREATE and emits a structured `write_edges` log (written/dropped/invalid + per-edge reason via `write_edge_rejected`) — no silent drop — returning a `WriteEdgesResult` (`int()`-coercible to `written`). `write_nodes` de-dups cross-turn references by id (a prior-graph id present in the subgraph is reused, not re-minted) and logs `write_nodes created=N reused=M`; reused nodes are NOT counted as added. Both share one scoped existence read (`_existing_node_ids`). As of **WU-3C1**, `write_nodes` also takes optional keyword-only `user_id`/`search_space_id` (server-injected Layer-2 node scoping, `None`-omitted) and always stamps a `created_at` ISO-8601 UTC prop; `stamp_graded_at(*, attempt_id, ts=None) -> int` sets `graded_at` on every node of the frozen subgraph at Done (idempotent overwrite; raises `RetentionError` on Neo4j failure; `_record_to_node` strips all four metadata props so `read_graph` round-trips byte-identically). **WU-5A2 back-compat widening:** the optional `ts: str | datetime | None` lets the Done handler thread ONE captured `done_ts` so Neo4j `graded_at` and Postgres `last_evidence_at` carry the IDENTICAL instant (a `datetime` is `.isoformat()`'d, a string passes through verbatim, `None` falls back to `_utc_now_iso()` — the two pre-existing callers stay valid). **WU-4C1** adds `read_node_created_at(*, attempt_id) -> dict[node_id, created_at_iso]` — a tiny read-only helper returning each `:_KGNode`'s `created_at` (omitting nulls), the per-turn temporal signal `read_graph` strips; `done_turn_order.build_turn_order` consumes it (NOT a schema change). **WU-5B3a-0** adds the sibling `read_node_graded_at(*, attempt_id) -> dict[node_id, graded_at_iso]` (mirrors `read_node_created_at`; None-omit; `{}` on an unstamped/empty subgraph) — the durable `done_ts` source for the retry janitor (there is NO Postgres `graded_at` column; `read_graph` strips `graded_at` too), the raw ISO-8601 string the janitor parses tz-aware via `datetime.fromisoformat`. **`canon_projection.py`** (WU-3C1) is the `:Canon` projection seeder: it reads Layer-1 `apollo_kg_entities` from Postgres and idempotently `MERGE`s `:Canon` Neo4j nodes keyed on `key = entity.id` (the BIGSERIAL surrogate id — load-bearing: it prevents two concepts that both mint the same `canonical_key` from fusing into one node and cross-contaminating future `RESOLVES_TO` edges), carrying `search_space_id`/`concept_id`/`canonical_key`/`kind`/`display_name`. Misconception entities ARE projected; the projection is course-scoped (`concept_id` or `search_space_id`; refuses an unscoped global seed), write-only, and rebuildable from Postgres at any time (never authored in Neo4j). Pure split: `CanonNodeSpec`/`entity_to_canon_spec`/`canon_spec_to_row` (DB-free mapping) + `load_entity_specs`/`merge_specs`/`project_canon` (async seeder). The §5 resolver, `RESOLVES_TO` edges, and `:Canon` reads are **delivered in WU-3C2** (`apollo/resolution/` + `resolution_store.py`). **`resolution_store.py`** (WU-3C2) is the persistence half of the resolver: it writes `(:_KGNode)-[:RESOLVES_TO {method,confidence,resolved_at}]->(:Canon)` edges (idempotent `MERGE` — a re-run overwrites props, never duplicates) and persists the four Layer-2 resolution node-fields (`resolution`/`resolved_key`/`resolution_method`/`resolution_confidence`) via an idempotent `SET` (`None`-omitting `resolved_key`); `store._record_to_node` now ALSO strips those four props so `read_graph` round-trips byte-identically once resolution has stamped them. `RESOLVES_TO` is a `:_KGNode→:Canon` CROSS-LABEL edge written by its own Cypher — deliberately NOT a member of `EdgeType`/`EDGE_ALLOWED_PAIRS` (those constrain within-subgraph `:_KGNode→:_KGNode` edges written through `store.write_edges`). Pure mapping seams (`resolved_node_to_edge_spec`/`resolved_node_to_field_spec`) + async writers (`write_resolves_to`/`persist_resolution_fields`/`write_resolution`). |
| `apollo/resolution/` | `candidates.py`, `result.py`, `tiers.py`, `structural.py`, `competition.py`, `assignment.py`, `resolver.py`, `equation_alignment.py`, `embedding.py`, `nli_config.py`, `nli_adjudicator.py`, `polarity.py`, `semantic_shortlist.py`, `nli_resolution.py`, `calibration.py` | The **§5 shared reference-anchored resolver** (WU-3C2), STANDALONE so WU-4A's `graph_compare` imports it (`from apollo.resolution import resolve_attempt`) rather than owning it. `resolve_attempt(student_graph, candidates, *, confirmed_resolutions=None, fuzzy_threshold=0.9, symbolic_mappings=None) -> ResolutionResult` maps each student evidence node onto a CLOSED candidate set (this problem's reference nodes + course `misc.*`, built by `build_candidate_set` + the `candidates_from_reference_solution`/`candidates_from_misconceptions` adapters) via content-first tiers (exact → SymPy-symbolic REUSING `sympy_exec.parse_zero_form`, sign-exact → normalized alias → RapidFuzz `token_set_ratio` ≥ 0.9, the only RapidFuzz site). Node-recovery adds two precision-bounded tiers ahead of fuzzy: a **derived equation-alignment** tier (`equation_alignment.py`, cap 0.95, symbolic-only, no numeric-coincidence credit) and a **Phase 1b exact-only alias channel** (`Candidate.exact_aliases`, cap 0.92, matched exact-normalized only and DELIBERATELY never fuzzed; populated from a reference step's `content.aliases`, default `()` keeps grades byte-identical, SHADOW-gated). **Symbolic mappings are PER-PROBLEM declared data, NOT a global default:** `symbolic_mappings` defaults to `None` → `{}` (no substitution); the §6.9 `d=2r` circular-area equivalence resolves only when the caller passes `symbolic_mappings={'d':'2*r'}` (WU-4A supplies the per-problem table). The structural / anti-over-normalization signals the resolver actually wires are the **type-compat HARD constraint** (`condition↔condition` only) + **misconception competition** ranked on **RAW lexical proximity** (1.0 for an exact-alias hit, the `token_set_ratio` for a fuzzy hit — the §3 method cap is the *reported* confidence, re-derived downstream, never the competition signal): `tiers.match_alias_all`/`match_fuzzy_all` surface EVERY type-compatible above-threshold candidate (each carrying its raw score + winning alias) so a competing misconception is never discarded before competition (a polar near-miss out-competes the lexically-close reference node, §6.11), and a **per-winning-alias polarity/direction screen** rejects only a direction-inverted match on the alias that produced the fuzzy hit (an unrelated inverted alias on the same candidate no longer false-rejects a valid match; misconceptions are exempt — they are supposed to be polar). Each candidate enters the lexical competition **once**: `_content_match` dedupes by candidate and keeps the higher tier EXPLICITLY (alias 0.92 > fuzzy 0.80), so a candidate that exact-alias-matches (raw 1.0) *and* fuzzy-matches itself (token_set_ratio of identical strings == 1.0) reports `alias` deterministically, never order-/tie-dependent on the competition list. **Neighborhood corroboration (§5 steps 2-3) is DEFERRED** — v1 wires type-compat + competition only; the `propagate_and_veto` seam is unbuilt (a WU-4A-era refinement), so `structural.py` carries ONLY `type_compatible` + the `ScoredMatch` dataclass (no neighborhood-boost helper). Then **bounded greedy global assignment** (many students→one reference allowed; one student never splits; cap 150 student nodes → whole-attempt abstention, no hang). **Task 4 (2026-06-29) retired the silent one-LLM-adjudication path** (`adjudication.py` deleted): a post-tier, non-clarified node stays `unresolved` DATA (no LLM guess); `result.llm_calls` is always 0; the clarification loop (Task 5+) now occupies that band. Per-node output `{resolution, resolved_key, resolution_method, resolution_confidence}` with confidence caps by method (exact 1.0 / symbolic 0.98 / derived 0.95 / alias 0.92 / **clarification 0.90** (Task 3 / §5.3 — authoritative confirmed answer, applied before tiers, type-compat enforced) / fuzzy 0.80 / LLM 0.75 (persisted rows; no live path) / unresolved 0.0, the §3 damper input). `confirmed_resolutions: dict[str,str] | None = None` maps `node_id → candidate_key` for nodes whose mapping was authorised by a live clarification exchange; a type-incompatible or unknown key is silently ignored (node follows the normal tier path). PURE + deterministic (re-runs yield identical results); a non-match is `unresolved` DATA (no edge, no exception). The resolver does NOT grade, simulate, persist, or orchestrate Done — matching only (persistence is `resolution_store.py`; grading is WU-4A). **NLI tier (Tasks 11–12, DORMANT — default OFF):** `nli_resolution.py::match_nli_semantic` is a RECALL-ONLY FALLBACK that runs after the entire fused lexical tier (exact/symbolic/derived/alias/clarification/fuzzy) finds nothing — it can therefore never mask a lexical-level misconception, only recover under-resolved paraphrase nodes. **Misconception NLI competition against fuzzy lexical winners (2026-07-05 routing Fix 2, behind `APOLLO_NLI_MISC_POSITIVE_CERTIFY`, default OFF):** the pure recall-only contract had a diagnosed hole (`.superpowers/sdd/misc-node-routing-diagnosis.md` Q2, the frozen-baseline `control_credit_leak` defect): a wrong-claim node that FALSELY alias/fuzzy-matches a lexically-close REFERENCE candidate short-circuits at the lexical tier and its misconception NLI check never runs — the student gets undeserved credit AND the misconception goes undetected. With the flag ON and NLI active, `_content_match` now intercepts a NON-misconception fused-lexical (alias/fuzzy) winner BEFORE returning it and runs `nli_resolution.py::match_nli_misconception_certify` (misconception-only shortlist → polarity screen → NLI classify) against the node's type-compatible `misc.*` candidates; a misconception entailing ≥ `misc_certify_entailment` WINS the node (`ScoredMatch(…, "nli", 0.88)` → §6.2 contradiction, no credit) instead of the lexical credit. EXACT/symbolic/derived/clarification-tier winners return earlier in `_content_match` and are NEVER intercepted — only sub-exact (alias/fuzzy) winners can be out-competed, and only by a high-entailment certify. Flag OFF (default) is byte-identical: the lexical winner returns untouched and the competition function is never called. Applies only to `NLI_NODE_TYPES = {procedure_step, condition, definition, simplification}` (equation and variable_mapping are excluded — the deterministic tiers already cover them). The composer flow: semantic shortlist (embedding cosine when an embedder is present, else lexical Jaccard over `candidate_surface_texts`, whose first surface is the candidate's `display_name` = a reference step's `content.label` else the canonical key) narrows candidates to top-K → polarity screen (`polarity.py`, rejects direction-inverted matches; a bounded-window litotes guard `_LITOTES_WINDOW=3` lets "no <noun> change" ≡ "constant" pass to NLI while a distant negation still fires) → positive content-overlap floor (shared non-trivial tokens required) → NLI classify via `NLIAdjudicator.classify(premise, hypothesis)` → accept on `entailment ≥ min_entailment AND contradiction ≤ max_contradiction` (PER-MODEL tuned defaults — large `0.90`/`0.05`, small `0.70`/`0.10`); misconception SEMANTIC VETO runs FIRST (if the student surface entails a paraphrased misconception at ≥ `misconception_veto_entailment` — per-model `0.98` large / `0.96` small — credit is denied regardless of reference matches). **Misconception POSITIVE-CERTIFY (2026-07-04, behind `APOLLO_NLI_MISC_POSITIVE_CERTIFY`, default OFF):** the veto branch was VETO-ONLY — it blocked reference credit but never resolved the node TO the entailed `misc.*` candidate, so only near-verbatim lexical `trigger_phrases` could positively detect a misconception (0/8 on control personas, control issue #82). With the flag ON (`config/settings.py::apollo_nli_misc_positive_certify()`, threaded as `NLIParams.misc_positive_certify` via `load_nli_params()`), the SAME entailment ≥ `misconception_veto_entailment` positively resolves the node to the `misc.*` candidate — `ScoredMatch(node_id, misc_candidate, "nli", 0.88)`, symmetric to the reference certify, feeding the §6.2 `misc.*`-prefix contradiction detection. **Certify bar split from the veto bar (2026-07-05 routing Fix 3):** the CERTIFY decision now reads its own `NLIParams.misc_certify_entailment` (env `APOLLO_NLI_MISC_CERTIFY_ENTAILMENT`, default 0.95 — a real control-persona misconception utterance measured max entailment 0.9742, just under the 0.98 veto bar), while the VETO decision keeps `misconception_veto_entailment` unchanged (0.98 large / 0.96 small); the same bar drives the Fix-2 resolver-level competition below. If an operator sets the certify bar above the veto bar, an entailment between the two still vetoes (reference credit stays blocked). Flag OFF never reads the certify bar — veto-only behavior is byte-identical. The veto side-effect is preserved in BOTH flag states (reference credit stays blocked); flag OFF is byte-identical veto-only behavior, and flipping it ON is a grading-behavior change reserved for a human decision; ambiguity guard: if top-2 entailment scores are within `ambiguity_margin (0.10)`, the function abstains (`→ None`). Accepted match: `ScoredMatch(node_id, candidate, "nli", 0.88)` (cap 0.88, between clarification@0.90 and fuzzy@0.80). Shared embedding primitives live in `embedding.py` (neutral module); `apollo/clarification/embedding.py` is now a re-export shim. `calibration.py` holds the dev-set harness (`sweep_thresholds` + `best_operating_point(report, min_precision)`) used to determine calibrated thresholds before enabling the tier. **Calibration has RUN (2026-07-01, both checkpoints — `docs/_archive/experiments/2026-07-01-nli-threshold-tuning`): precision 1.000 with zero false credits on the dev set, end-to-end resolve_attempt gate PASS for both.** **The tier is now DEFAULT-ON (2026-07-01 — human enablement decision, validated in SHADOW):** `transformers`/`torch`/`sentencepiece` moved INTO the main `requirements.txt` (CPU-only via `--extra-index-url https://download.pytorch.org/whl/cpu` so the image stays slim; the large checkpoint downloads on first grade). `requirements-nli.txt` is retained only for the historical Windows-wheel note. Flags: `APOLLO_NLI_ENABLED` (**default ON**; `nli_config.nli_enabled()` returns True when unset — set `=0`/`false`/`no` as the KILL SWITCH), `APOLLO_NLI_MODEL` (default `cross-encoder/nli-deberta-v3-large` — the tuned production target; resolved by `active_nli_model()`), `APOLLO_NLI_CHAT_MAX_NODES` (default 15; over-cap turns skip NLI), `APOLLO_NLI_GRADING_MAX_NODES` (default **15** — the cap is a binary whole-attempt NLI disable, not a per-node truncation, and 15 sits below realistic attempt sizes (~25 nodes); over-cap grading attempts skip NLI entirely. 2026-07-05 routing Fix 1, revised after PR #101 review: the DEFAULT deliberately stays 15 because raising it is an un-gated grading-behavior change under default-ON NLI (measured f1c drift: 6 attempts' unresolved_rate/composite move) — campaign/probe runs OPT IN via the env override `APOLLO_NLI_GRADING_MAX_NODES=40` (`campaign/infra/env.campaign.example`), snapshot-audited in every frozen campaign config via `campaign/config.py`'s `int_flags`). CAVEAT (honest): the calibration dev set is AUTHORED, not yet validated on real graded attempts — enablement is a SHADOW rollout; roll back via the flag. **Thresholds are now PER-MODEL** (`default_params_for_model`): large `min_entailment=0.90`/`max_contradiction=0.05`/`misconception_veto_entailment=0.98`, small `0.70`/`0.10`/`0.96`, an unknown checkpoint → a SAFE fallback (veto ≥ 0.96 — the class-default `0.80` would false-veto correct students, tuning §3). `load_nli_params()` resolves the ACTIVE model's tuned defaults then applies any `APOLLO_NLI_*` env override on top; the frozen `NLIParams` field defaults (`top_k=5`/`0.87`/`0.10`/`0.10`/`0.80`) are NEUTRAL construction defaults (used by `best_operating_point`/tests), NOT the production floors. |
| `apollo/provisioning/` | `__init__.py`, `promotion_lint.py`, `problem_hash.py`, `dedup.py`, `dedup_constants.py`, `scrape.py`, `tag_mint.py`, `tag_mint_persist.py`, `solution.py`, `pairing_gate.py`, `queue.py`, `metered_chat.py`, `cost_constants.py`, `enqueue.py`, `orchestrator.py`, `promote.py`, `ingest.py`, `provisioning_schema.py`, `retrieval_adapter.py` | **WU-3B2c — the §8B.5 course-local dedup ladder.** `resolve_candidate(db, *, search_space_id, concept_id, candidate, embed_fn, judge_fn, ingest_run_id=None, exclude_entity_ids=None) -> DedupVerdict(verdict, method, similarity, matched_entity_id)` resolves ONE candidate against THIS course's `apollo_kg_entities` inventory, running slug-exact → `scope_summary`-embedding cosine → injected LLM-judge, scoped to the candidate's `concept_id` WITHIN `Subject.search_space_id` (both WHEREs applied in SQL BEFORE any cosine; PR2 added the concept filter + a same-mint `exclude_entity_ids` so neither cross-concept/foreign-set nor within-problem entities fuse; `_in_course_entities` is the sole candidate path and applies the predicates first), first-writer-wins (lowest `KGEntity.id` breaks cosine ties — the earliest writer owns the vocabulary), writing exactly ONE `apollo_dedup_decisions` row per resolution (`method`=slug/embedding/llm_judge, `similarity`=cosine for the embedding/judge tiers else NULL, `candidate_key`=the candidate slug, `ingest_run_id` stamped only when the caller supplies it). Embedding source is the on-the-fly-embedded `KGEntity.scope_summary` (NO persisted vector; a NULL summary is skipped by the embedding tier); `embed_fn` (SYNC `Callable[[str], Sequence[float]]`, inject `embed_text`) / `judge_fn` (SYNC `Callable[..., str] -> 'merged'|'distinct'`, inject a `cheap_chat` adapter owning the prompt+parse) are param-injected so Tier-1 tests are network-free (3B2d/3B2f own the real wiring). Bands `EMBED_MERGE_THRESHOLD=0.92` (inclusive merge) / `EMBED_JUDGE_BAND=(0.82, 0.92)` (lower-inclusive escalate-to-judge band; `<0.82` distinct) live in `dedup_constants.py` (env-overridable, defaults pinned by ADJ #4). This unit reads the inventory + writes the audit row ONLY — it does NOT scrape/mint/upsert entities or problems (3B2d) and does NOT increment `apollo_ingest_runs.n_dedup_merged` (3B2g). **WU-3B2b — the §8B.4 PURE 9-gate promotion lint (the auto-provisioning SAFETY CORE; no LLM/DB/Neo4j/container/migration).** `run_promotion_lint(graph, *, canonical_symbols, normalization_map, existing_problem_hashes, active_gates=ALL_PROMOTION_GATES) -> PromotionResult(ok, failed_gate, diagnostic)` runs the nine gates IN ORDER, short-circuiting on first failure; the CALLER (`promote`) passes a CONTENT-DERIVED `active_gates` from `content_active_gates(graph)` — structural core {1,2,3,5,8} always, symbolic rigor {4,6,7} only when a parseable equation is present, and solve/check {9} only when a parseable governing system plus a target-isolating stated answer exist (subject-agnostic, design `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-26-subject-agnostic-promotion-gates-design.md`). Gates: (1) schema — `Problem.model_validate` + every edge in `EDGE_ALLOWED_PAIRS` (via `to_kg_graph`) + a mint-map-membership sub-check (any `entry_type` ∉ the frozen `_ENTRY_TYPE_TO_KIND_PREFIX` fails CLOSED — ADJ #5 defense-in-depth); ALWAYS runs (it builds the `Problem`+`KGGraph`); (2) reference closure — `validate_reference_graph` VERBATIM (§6.1); (3) DAG — `KGGraph.topological_order(DEPENDS_ON)` raises on cycle; (4) symbol consistency — the SOLE foreign-symbol guard (gate 6 does NOT reject foreign symbols), reading the PASSED-IN `canonical_symbols`/`normalization_map`. On the SEEDED-table path a symbol is non-foreign iff it normalizes via the table OR the problem's AUTHOR grounds it (`_author_grounded_symbols` = given / STRUCTURALLY declared via a definition|variable_mapping `symbol`/`term` field (`_declared_symbols`) / coupling-intermediate / cancelled — the DECLARED grounding, EXCLUDING both the speculative lone graph-derived answer term AND any free-prose `meaning`/`definition` token; grounding off prose would admit a garbage OCR token that appears in both an equation and a sentence, the WU-AAS lane B2.2 Finding 2 over-acceptance — the lenient prose path `_defined_symbols` is confined to the TABLE-LESS branch where gate 7's under-determination check is the real guard); this author-grounding arm (WU-AAS lane B2.2 / G4.2, F1a Finding B) is PURELY ADDITIVE — the 41 seeded symbols all normalize so their verdicts are byte-identical, and it fixes a prose-minted problem mis-filed under a seeded table (e.g. a kinematics `x`/`varmap.var_x` under a fluid table) whose own varmap/given grounds the symbol (an ungrounded left-over is still rejected here or falls to gate 7). When NO table exists (a fresh auto-minted concept) it grounds each symbol against the problem's OWN closure (`_internal_grounded_symbols` = `_author_grounded_symbols` PLUS the lone graph-derived answer, SUPERSET-accept) and the prose `target_unknown` is NO LONGER added; (5) procedure coherence — a kind-AGNOSTIC graph property (spec §4.1): the structural head + chain-coverage (unique terminal sink) ALWAYS runs, and the symbolic half self-activates on a parseable terminal equation to check it computes the single GRAPH-DERIVED answer (`_derive_symbolic_answer`, NOT the prose target); (6) SymPy parse — `parse_zero_form` catches MALFORMED syntax only, and TOLERATES two mainstream teacher-PDF notations (WU-AAS lane B2.2 / G4.2, F1a Findings A/B): a CHAINED equality (`symbol = symbolic-formula = numeric-substitution = final`) is normalized to its FIRST equality (the symbolic statement; the trailing `= C = D` numeric/unit tail is DISCARDED — debug-logged `sympy_parse_chained_equality_normalized`, never raised — the safe under-constrain direction, gate 7 catches any resulting openness), and `^` is normalized to `Pow` via `convert_xor` instead of raising SymPy's XOR type error. `parse_zero_form` is the SINGLE equation parser (WU-AAS lane B2.2 Finding 1): the resolution tier (`apollo.resolution.tiers._zero_form`) DELEGATES to it (passing its own extended locals, swallowing `MalformedEquationError`→`None` to keep the non-crash contract) rather than re-implementing the split/parse — so a minted subject's stored `symbolic` (which may carry `^`/chained forms) and the runtime grader parse IDENTICAL notations, closing a recall gap where the resolver's old duplicate parser returned None on those forms; (7) equation-system closure (Option 2) — a PAPER check: closed iff the graph-derived answer is ≤ 1 unknown, `> 1` is under-determined → reject (NOT an end-to-end solve; honest v1 limit §8B.4:1347; the per-problem quarantine 3B2h is the runtime catch); (8) duplicate — `problem_dup_hash(problem)` ∉ the caller-supplied concept-scoped `existing_problem_hashes`; (9) solve/check — solve the governing residual system under given/bound/cancelled/assumption-bearing knowns, compare the solved target with the separately stated answer by `simplify(solved-stated) == 0`, then use pole/domain-avoiding numeric samples only when symbolic comparison is inconclusive. Gate 9 returns a typed `verified` pass, `refuted` failure with solved-vs-stated evidence, or `unresolved` non-pass on parse/unsupported/underdetermined/timeout conditions; authored sets map unresolved to their existing `held_for_review` lane while older callers keep treating it as failure. PURE + fixture-tested (legacy Bernoulli/AAE compatibility + correct/wrong/unresolved gate-9 corpus checks + one discriminating adversarial per legacy gate asserting `failed_gate==N` + short-circuit-order + the DIFFERENTIAL anchor old≡new + the 6 AAE 333 fixtures promoting). 3B2b owns the gate logic + diagnostic ONLY — it does NOT promote, call `project_canon`, write `rejected_problems`, or touch the DB; the `PromotionResult` → promote/reject mapping is 3B2g's, with authored-set unresolved results mapped to held review. Mirrors `apollo/resolution/` (standalone, re-export `__init__`). **WU-3B2d — the LLM-bearing front of §8B (stage 1 scrape + stage 4 tag/mint; the injected `chat_fn`/`embed_fn` are network-free in Tier-1, mocked).** `scrape.py`: `scrape_questions(chunks, *, chat_fn) -> ScrapeResult(candidates, scraped_count, parse_failures)` runs one `chat_fn` pass PER `AITAChunk` (READ ONLY — NEVER re-indexes) into typed `CandidateQuestion`s (provenance + LLM `difficulty` validated against `Problem.Difficulty`); a malformed/empty JSON or an invalid candidate is a fail-SOFT per-chunk drop counted in `parse_failures` (never a half-parsed row). `write_tier1_problems(db, candidates, *, concept_id, search_space_id) -> int` persists them as **Tier-1 inventory** — `tier=1` EXPLICIT (the SAFETY TRAP: the ORM `tier` default is 2/teachable, so an omitted explicit value would silently make scraped inventory selectable; `test_tier1_row_excluded_by_selector` proves `list_problems_for_concept` excludes a Tier-1 row), `provenance={document_id, page, chunk_content_hash}`, denormalized `search_space_id`. **Idempotency** keys on a CONTENT hash (`chunk_content_hash = sha256(_normalize(content))` — collapse-whitespace/strip/lowercase, NOT the volatile `aita_chunks.id`, so a re-index is a no-op) folded into a deterministic `problem_code = f"scrape.{hash}"`; the writer SELECTs `(concept_id, problem_code)`-then-skips (the seed-script `_upsert_entity` pattern — the create_all test ORM does not declare migration-018's `UNIQUE (concept_id, problem_code)`, so application-level dedup is the portable guard; a re-run inserts ZERO rows; dropping the guard duplicates rows). The NOT-NULL `concept_id` SEAM is resolved by `resolve_or_create_provisional_concept` — a reserved per-course `provisional.inventory` concept (empty `canonical_symbols`, never teachable because its rows are tier=1; stage-4 re-homes a promoted problem onto its real tagged concept). `tag_mint.py`: `tag_and_mint(db, pair, *, chat_fn, embed_fn) -> MintPlan` consumes an ALREADY-approved `ApprovedPair` (3B2e produces a compatible value LATER; tested here with a hand-built fixture — this unit does NOT find/generate/pair solutions), LLM-drafts the concept tag (slug→BIGINT via `resolve_or_create_concept`, creating the concept if absent — the §6 namespace contract keys ALL persistence on the BIGINT, never the slug) + prereq edges, **AUTHORS** `apollo_concepts.canonical_symbols`/`normalization_map` first-writer-wins UNION from the approved problem's `given_values` keys + `target_unknown` + equation free-symbols (each reduced to its subscript base, `P1`/`P2`→`P` — so a 3B2b gate-4 over the minted concept is NON-VACUOUS; a later DIFFERENT problem UNIONs new symbols but NEVER rewrites the first writer's, §8B.5; STORED in the `CanonicalSymbols`-validatable shape `{"symbols": [...], "description": {}}` -- the same shape the registry seed writes -- so an authored concept round-trips through the runtime reader `apollo.subjects.curriculum_db.load_concept_definition` -> `CanonicalSymbols.model_validate` (hit on every teaching session); NOT a flat `{symbol: True}` map), then mints reference + misconception `EntitySpec`s by REUSING two frozen seed converters (`reference_solution_to_entities`/`misconceptions_to_entities` — IMPORTED, not reimplemented; prereqs come from the LLM tag draft, NOT `concept_dag_to_prereqs`, and `annotate_reference_solution` is a promotion-time step owned by 3B2g, so both are intentionally UNUSED here), resolving EACH entity candidate through 3B2c's `resolve_candidate` BEFORE upsert (a `merged` verdict reuses the matched id, recorded in `MintPlan.merged_entity_keys`; a `distinct` verdict upserts on `(concept_id, canonical_key)` + authors `scope_summary` from `display_name`+symbols). **Misconception-storage DEVIATION (orchestrator-signed, ADJ #2):** auto-minted misconceptions are stored as `apollo_kg_entities kind='misconception'` carrying `payload['opposes_entity_key']`/`opposes_entity_id` (via the frozen `misconceptions_to_entities` + a second-pass `link_opposes`) — NOT the literal §8B.2 `apollo_misconceptions` table (whose NOT-NULL Socratic `probe_question`/`rt_steps` v1 auto-provisioning cannot responsibly author; the runtime `opposes_map` is structurally empty in v1, so that channel is dormant; `test_minted_misconception_is_kg_entity` asserts NO `apollo_misconceptions` write). FAIL-CLOSED: a hallucinated/unmappable LLM tag or an `opposes_entity_key` resolving to no entity raises `TagMintError` (mirrors `SeedError`'s NO-FALLBACK convention — a mislinked entity silently corrupts grading for every student) and the caller marks the run failed (the caller owns the transaction; no partial mint commits). EXCEPTION (2026-06-30): a prereq draft edge naming an unminted key is DROPPED (logged `tag_mint_dropped_unresolvable_prereqs`), not fatal — prereqs are optional KG enrichment the LLM routinely draws to a problem given. NO promotion here — 3B2g runs `run_promotion_lint` over the `MintPlan`, flips Tier-2, projects `:Canon`. The persistence write helpers (`resolve_or_create_concept`/`author_concept_symbols`/`upsert_entity`/`link_opposes`/`insert_prereqs`) live in `tag_mint_persist.py` (PARALLELED from `scripts/seed_apollo_learner_model.py`, generalized off the hardcoded bernoulli slug; the seed script is WRAPPED, not imported). **Prompt↔parser contract is machine-checkable (WU-3B2x):** the stage-1/2/4 LLM prompts now declare their EXACT output schema via `provisioning_schema.build_solution_schema()`/`build_tag_schema()` (derived FROM `ReferenceStep.model_fields`/`NODE_CONTENT_TYPES` so the schema can never drift from the parser), and deterministic no-network contract tests in `tests/test_provisioning_schema.py` pin the declared schema to the Pydantic models (the test that would have caught the original generation stubs). **WU-3B2e — the §8B "solution lifecycle" (stage 2 find-or-generate + stage 3 pairing/correctness gate; LLM-bearing but network-free in Tier-1, every callable injected + mocked).** `solution.py`: `find_or_generate(db, question, *, retrieve_fn, chat_fn) -> ReferenceSolutionDraft` retrieve-FIRST (a retrieved span flagged `carries_solution=True` → an extraction `chat_fn` pass → `solution_source='extracted'`, grounding = the retrieved spans) then RAG-grounded GENERATE fallback (`chat_fn` over the question + the SAME retrieved spans-as-context → `solution_source='generated'`, grounding carries those spans so the stage-3 Phase-B judge has real context to entail against — the §8B.2 "ground both in retrieved passages" requirement). The generated `reference_solution` is `Problem.model_validate`-checked BEFORE a draft returns; a retrieve-empty + unparseable/empty/Problem-invalid generate raises `SolutionDraftError` (FAIL-CLOSED — NEVER an empty-step draft; `Problem` requires `reference_solution` min_length=1). `solution_hash(draft)` = `sha256` over the canonical-JSON `reference_solution` (the downstream `(chunk_content_hash, solution_hash)` idempotency key 3B2g writes on; deterministic + path-independent). `build_approved_pair(question, draft, *, search_space_id) -> tag_mint.ApprovedPair` assembles the `Problem`-validatable `problem` dict + stamps `solution_source` from the draft, IMPORTING the REAL `ApprovedPair` (round-trip pinned, NEVER mocked). `pairing_gate.py`: `validate_pair(question, draft, *, retrieve_fn, judge_fn) -> PairingVerdict(paired, faithful, failed_claims, confidence)` runs a two-phase span-grounded judge over the SAME grounding the generator used (`draft.grounding`, else re-grounds via `retrieve_fn`) — Phase A pairing/answer-relevance (short-circuits Phase B when not paired) then Phase B claim-decomposed faithfulness (any unentailed claim → `faithful=False` with `failed_claims`). **FAIL-CLOSED, the EXPLICIT INVERSION of `leakage_judge.py:126-129`'s fail-OPEN** — a malformed/non-JSON/exception/non-object judge response at EITHER phase ⇒ `PairingVerdict(paired=False, faithful=False, failed_claims=("<unparseable judge response>",), confidence=0.0)`, NEVER an approval; ALL `judge_fn` calls route through ONE private `_judge_or_fail_closed` so the fail-closed default lives in a single place. `rejection_from_verdict(verdict) -> Rejection | None` is the single fail-mapping point (None on approved; else `reason ∈ {'unparseable_judge','not_paired','unfaithful_claims'}`). It logs ONE structured `pairing_verdict` line (counts + booleans + `solution_source` ONLY — NO solution/question/passage text, NO PII). This unit makes NO DB write and reads NO learner state (inputs are COURSE MATERIAL only); it does NOT mint (3B2d), promote/lint or write `rejected_problems` (3B2g), or meter/queue (3B2f) — it hands typed `ReferenceSolutionDraft`/`PairingVerdict`/`Rejection`/`SolutionDraftError` values UP. The stage-2/stage-3 public surface (`find_or_generate`/`solution_hash`/`build_approved_pair`/`GroundingSpan`/`ReferenceSolutionDraft`/`SolutionDraftError`, `validate_pair`/`rejection_from_verdict`/`PairingVerdict`/`Rejection`) is RE-EXPORTED from `apollo/provisioning/__init__.py`. **WU-3B2f — the §8B concurrency + cost spine (the claim/lease queue drain + the per-call metered LLM client; the orchestrator/worker/enqueue that CONSUME them are 3B2g).** `queue.py`: `claim_provisioning_job(session, *, lease_owner, lease_seconds) -> ClaimedJob | None` is the SKIP-LOCKED claim/lease drain over `apollo_provisioning_jobs` (mirrors `knowledge/teacher_weekly.py:_claim_upload_job_async`) — `SELECT … WHERE state='pending' OR (state='running' AND lease_expires_at < now()) ORDER BY created_at, id FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED LIMIT 1`, then on a row flips `state='running'`, sets `lease_owner`/`lease_expires_at=now()+lease_seconds`, bumps `attempt_count += 1`, and COMMITs (claim-then-commit-before-work, matching `learner_janitor._claim_due`; `now()` is Python-side `datetime.now(UTC)`). `complete_job(session, *, job_id)` → terminal `completed` + lease cleared; `fail_job(session, *, job_id, error) -> 'failed'|'pending'` dead-letters to `failed` when `attempt_count >= MAX_ATTEMPTS` else retries to `pending` (always clears the lease + sets `last_error`); `release_job(session, *, job_id)` cooperatively returns a job to `pending` with `attempt_count` UNCHANGED. The frozen `ClaimedJob(job_id, search_space_id, document_id, ingest_run_id, attempt_count)` carries the post-bump attempt count. The provisioning `state` vocabulary is `pending/running/completed/failed` — DISTINCT from the run `status` vocabulary (`queued/running/succeeded/failed`). The `skip_locked=True` clause provides NON-BLOCKING LIVENESS (a worker SKIPS an already-locked row instead of head-of-line blocking on it) and is mutation-proven by `test_skip_locked_skips_locked_row_without_blocking` in `tests/database/test_apollo_provisioning_queue.py` (an externally-held row lock makes a no-skip claim block until it times out → REDs). Non-overlap (no double-claim) is guaranteed by `FOR UPDATE` ALONE — the loser blocks, then EvalPlanQual rechecks the now-`running` row, finds it no longer matches the pending/expired predicate, and excludes it — so the two-worker non-overlap tests intentionally do NOT discriminate `skip_locked` (they pin the non-overlap invariant, not the liveness clause). `metered_chat.py`: `MeteredChat(ingest_run, *, client=None, ceiling=PER_DOCUMENT_TOKEN_CEILING, document_id=None)` is the ONLY programmatic token signal in §8B — `apollo/agent/_llm.py` reads `response.usage` only to LOG it and DISCARDS it, so `MeteredChat` re-invokes the OpenAI client ITSELF (it does NOT import/mutate `_llm`), capturing usage and accumulating `llm_calls`/`llm_tokens_in`/`llm_tokens_out`/`llm_cost_usd` (`+=`, never overwrite) onto the passed `apollo_ingest_runs` ORM row (the durable per-document audit aggregate — the intended ORM write, NOT a value-object mutation). `.cheap`/`.main` are drop-in for the injected `chat_fn` (same `purpose=`/`messages=`/`response_format=`/`temperature=`/`model=` shape as `cheap_chat`/`main_chat`, same `APOLLO_CHEAP_MODEL` default `gpt-4o-mini` / `MAIN_MODEL` default `gpt-4o` routing, explicit `model=` overrides); `.scrape_chat_fn(system_prompt)` returns a positional-string `chat_fn(chunk_content) -> str` for the `scrape.py:141` seam, routed cheap. After EACH call, when the cumulative (in+out) tokens exceed `ceiling` it raises `CostBudgetExceeded(tokens, ceiling, document_id)` (the breaching call's counts ARE recorded first) — the abort signal the orchestrator (3B2g) turns into an `apollo_ingest_errors` row + `apollo_ingest_runs.status='failed'` (proven end-to-end on real PG by the cost-abort queue test; the PRODUCTION write site is 3B2g). Logs token COUNTS/ids/model only — never prompt/completion bodies, never the API key. `cost_constants.py` (pure config, mirrors `dedup_constants.py`): `PER_DOCUMENT_TOKEN_CEILING=2_000_000` (a runaway CIRCUIT BREAKER, NOT a tight budget — the real control is `APOLLO_AUTOPROVISION_ENABLED` defaulting OFF), `MAX_ATTEMPTS=3` (the dead-letter cap), the `gpt-4o`($2.50/$10) / `gpt-4o-mini`($0.15/$0.60) per-1M `MODEL_PRICES` table, and `cost_usd_for(model, *, tokens_in, tokens_out) -> Decimal` (`Decimal` is load-bearing — the column is `NUMERIC(12,6)`; an unknown model returns `Decimal('0')` and never raises). Routing pinned scrape/judge→cheap, generate→main (the orchestrator decides per stage, NOT this unit). All three names are RE-EXPORTED from `apollo/provisioning/__init__.py`. **WU-3B2g — the §8B orchestration spine (the LAST wiring unit of WU-3B2: it WIRES the already-built stages 3B2b–3B2f into the upload pipeline; it REDEFINES no stage and changes `apollo/handlers/done.py` NOT AT ALL).** `enqueue.py`: `enqueue_provisioning_job(session, *, search_space_id, document_id, content_hash) -> int | None` is the THIN content-key-idempotent enqueue at the indexing-completion seam (`knowledge/teacher_weekly.py` finalize block, riding the SAME commit so a job is never visible for a doc that did not finish indexing). Returns the new `apollo_provisioning_jobs.id`, or `None` when short-circuited: (a) the **content-hash short-circuit** (§9 OPS-2) — a SELECT finds a `status='succeeded'` `apollo_ingest_runs` row for `(document_id, content_hash)` ⇒ an unchanged re-upload enqueues ZERO new jobs (the mutation-discriminating property — removing the SELECT makes a duplicate job appear); (b) the **partial-unique-index collapse** — the migration-030 `apollo_provisioning_jobs_open_uniq` (`WHERE state IN ('pending','running')`) rejects a second OPEN insert with an `IntegrityError`. The ENTIRE enqueue runs inside ONE nested SAVEPOINT (`begin_nested`) and swallows ANY error (not just `IntegrityError`) → it can NEVER wedge the teacher-upload commit: a degraded env (e.g. the provisioning tables not yet migrated) rolls back ONLY the enqueue's own writes and returns `None`, leaving the upload-facing columns byte-identical (the §14 headline NON-REGRESSION). A `None` content_hash (legacy doc) cannot short-circuit (enqueues once). `orchestrator.py`: `run_provisioning(db, neo, *, job, metered_chat, embed_fn=None, retrieve_fn=None) -> ProvisioningOutcome(run_id, status, n_questions_scraped, n_promoted, n_rejected, n_dedup_merged)` drives the 6 stages for one claimed document (scrape+write_tier1 → per-candidate find_or_generate → validate_pair+rejection_from_verdict → build_approved_pair+tag_and_mint → promote), OWNING the `apollo_ingest_runs` lifecycle (queued→running+`started_at`→terminal succeeded|failed+`finished_at`; it NEVER leaves the run `'running'` — a per-document error always flips it terminal, §9 OPS-5, else the partial-unique-index wedges re-enqueue) and the §4b stage-outcome→observability decision: a per-CANDIDATE rejection (pairing `Rejection` / lint fail / a stage-2 `SolutionDraftError`) writes ONE `apollo_rejected_problems` row (`rejected_stage='pairing_gate'` with `failed_gate=NULL`, `='promotion_lint'` with the gate number, or `='solution_draft'` with `failed_gate=NULL` for an un-draftable candidate) and CONTINUES (`n_rejected` recomputed, the problem stays Tier-1); a per-DOCUMENT error (`TagMintError`/`CostBudgetExceeded`/`CanonProjectionError`/ANY unexpected exception via the catch-all `except Exception` mapping to `stage='orchestrator'`) writes ONE `apollo_ingest_errors(stage, error_class, context)` row and FAILS the whole run (the §8B "rejected ≠ errored" line). The per-run counters are ASSIGNED from freshly-computed values (never `+=`) so a re-claimed job's replay does not inflate them (§2c). It does NOT call `complete_job`/`fail_job` (the worker's terminal decision). `metered_chat.cheap`/`.main`/`.scrape_chat_fn(sys)` are the injected stage callables; `retrieve_fn` defaults to `retrieval_adapter.make_course_retrieve_fn(db, *, search_space_id, top_k=6)` — a course-scoped adapter that runs the existing hybrid search (pgvector + FTS over `aita_chunks` via `AITAHybridSearchRetriever`, course-scoped by `search_space_id` so grounding never crosses courses) and maps each chunk dict into an immutable `GroundingSpan` (`carries_solution=False` in v1; printed-solution extraction + span reranking are deferred follow-ups). This replaces the prior no-span stub that left the stage-3 faithfulness judge grounding on an empty string → every candidate rejected as `unfaithful_claims`. `promote.py`: `promote(db, neo, *, problem, mint_plan, search_space_id, concept_problem_id, existing_problem_hashes) -> PromoteResult(promoted, failed_gate, diagnostic)` is the promotion step — annotate the minted reference graph (`annotate_reference_solution`, frozen — `entity_key` per step via the §8 D5 `_entity_key_for_step` + `declared_paths`) → `run_promotion_lint(graph, canonical_symbols=<the concept's AUTHORED set>, normalization_map=<the concept's map>, existing_problem_hashes=…, active_gates=content_active_gates(annotated))` — the active set is CONTENT-DERIVED here (no stored subject profile, no `resolve_profile`); seeded-table gate 4 stays non-vacuous, gate 8 keyed on the passed dup-hash set. On PASS: store the COMPLETE annotated problem (`{**existing_payload, **annotated, "verification": …}` — the full `Problem`-validatable dict id/concept_id/difficulty/problem_text/given_values/target_unknown + the annotated `reference_solution`/`declared_paths`, REQUIRED because BOTH the student selector AND the gate-8 dup-hash validate `payload` through `Problem.model_validate`; the `verification` field stamps `"mechanically_verified"` when the symbolic rigor gates {4,6,7} were applicable and passed, else `"faithfulness_only"` — spec §5 honesty handle, additive/ignored by `Problem.model_validate`) into `apollo_concept_problems.payload`, **RE-HOME the row from the provisional-inventory concept onto the REAL tagged concept** (`row.concept_id = mint_plan.concept_id`) — `list_problems_for_concept` filters `concept_id == <session concept> AND tier == 2`, so a Tier-2 row left stranded under `provisional.inventory` is permanently UNREACHABLE; the re-home is exactly what scrape.py's "stage-4 re-homes a promoted problem onto its real tagged concept" means — flip `tier` 1→2 (keyed on the EXISTING row id, NEVER an insert), set `solution_source`, flush, then `project_canon(db, neo, search_space_id=…, concept_id=mint_plan.concept_id)` (idempotent `:Canon` MERGE). On FAIL: return `PromoteResult(promoted=False, failed_gate, diagnostic)` WITHOUT touching the row — `promote` does NOT write `apollo_rejected_problems` (the orchestrator is the SINGLE rejection-write owner). `promote` is idempotent (a re-run flips an already-Tier-2 row to 2 — a no-op — re-assigns the SAME tagged `concept_id`, and re-MERGEs `:Canon`); a `CanonProjectionError` is re-raised (the orchestrator maps it to an `apollo_ingest_errors` row + failed run; the already-flushed tier flip is left for idempotent re-projection on retry). **Stage-4 chat_fn seam (the wiring fix):** the orchestrator hands `tag_and_mint` a POSITIONAL-string adapter `lambda s: metered_chat.cheap(purpose='tag_mint', messages=[{role:'user',content:s}])` (mirroring `metered_chat.scrape_chat_fn`) because `_parse_tag` calls its `chat_fn(json.dumps(problem))` positionally while `MeteredChat.cheap` is keyword-only — handing `.cheap` directly would `TypeError` and promote nothing; `find_or_generate`/`validate_pair` call their callables WITH keywords so they consume `.main`/`.cheap` unchanged. **Gate-8 non-vacuity:** before `promote` the orchestrator computes the concept-scoped `existing_problem_hashes` by loading the already-promoted (`tier=2`) `apollo_concept_problems` payloads for `mint_plan.concept_id` and applying the frozen `problem_dup_hash` (an empty set would make gate 8 vacuous — a duplicate problem would always re-promote). **`n_dedup_merged`** = the sum of `len(mint_plan.merged_entity_keys)` over candidates that reached tag/mint (the real 3B2c dedup-merge count, no longer a v1-0 placeholder). **Audit-row accrual (observability note):** `apollo_rejected_problems`/`apollo_ingest_errors` rows are append-only and NOT idempotent across replays — a re-claimed/replayed job re-inserts them each run; the per-RUN COUNT COLUMNS (`n_rejected` etc.) are RE-ASSIGNED (not `+=`) so they never inflate, but the audit TABLES accrue duplicate rows across attempts for the same run (acceptable v1: counts are authoritative, the audit tables are human-inspectable history).
