promote to tier 2. Generated references (including every candidate when no
solution doc is paired), or OCR references that materially diverge from
generated cross-checks, stay tier 1 with
`ConceptProblem.provenance["authored_review"]` until a teacher approves. Held
problems do not run `tag_and_mint` or `promote`, so the canonical KG is not
mutated before approval.

**Ingestion observability (WU-AAS, lane G4.4).** `_run_set_background` opens one
`apollo_ingest_runs` row per ingestion (`IngestRun`, `status`
running→succeeded/failed, `started_at`/`finished_at`, `n_pages`,
`n_questions_scraped`/`n_promoted`/`n_rejected`), and the run is the SAME row
`MeteredChat` accrues LLM call/token/cost onto (so those aggregates persist instead
of being discarded on a throwaway namespace). Migration 043 adds the queryable
`dedup_pressure` JSONB gauge, updated inside `_record_decision` with total candidates,
exact merges, embedding merges/distincts, embedding merge share, and embedding
merges per concept. Both generic and authored terminal run logs include the complete
gauge, so abnormal false-merge pressure is visible without replaying audit rows.
**The run is opened AND committed
BEFORE indexing** (with `document_id=NULL`, migration 036) so that an OCR/indexing
stage failure — a bad PDF, or `index_authored_doc` raising "no chunks produced" —
still leaves a durable run row + `apollo_ingest_errors` row + whatever page evidence
was captured, instead of both tables staying EMPTY (the S2 "insufficient info"
failure class). Once problem indexing succeeds its document id is stamped onto the
run (the handle the GET surface looks up by; the queue path sets it at open).
`index_authored_doc` takes an optional `page_sink` that captures the transient
per-page OCR pass (`NormalizedPage` — text + confidence + extraction mode)
BEFORE its no-chunks guard, so a page-bearing-but-chunkless doc still surfaces its
OCR text on the failure path; the helpers in
`apollo/provisioning/authored_sets/observability.py`
(`start_ingest_run`/`persist_page_evidence`/`finalize_ingest_run`/`record_ingest_error`)
write one `apollo_ingest_page_evidence` row per source page (`IngestPageEvidence`:
role=`problem|solution`, `page_number`, `ocr_text`, `ocr_confidence`,
`extraction_mode`, and `verify_path_fired` set when a page's confidence is ≤ 0.6 —
the low-confidence signal the S2 audit reads; `document_id` NULLABLE for a page
captured before a doc was minted). On the SUCCESS path the page evidence + run
document id + `n_pages` are committed with the provisioning-status transition, so
the except handler re-persists evidence ONLY when that commit did not happen (no
duplicate rows); its run/error/evidence writes are committed explicitly, not via
`_set_status` (which early-returns uncommitted if the set row vanished). Before this,
both tables stayed EMPTY through a whole ingestion and no per-page OCR text was
persisted. The GET detail surface caps each page's `ocr_text` to
`_LIST_OCR_TEXT_CAP` (2000) chars with `ocr_text_truncated`/`ocr_text_chars` flags;
`?full_ocr=true` returns the untruncated body. Schema is migration
`036_apollo_ingest_page_evidence.sql`.

The mounted endpoints are teacher-gated with `require_user` +
`require_course_teacher` (role='teacher' membership; no auto-enroll
fallback — a plain course member 403s): `POST /apollo/authored-sets` accepts multipart
problem PDF (required) + solution PDF (optional) and starts in-process background provisioning,
`GET /apollo/authored-sets?search_space_id=` lists set statuses,
`GET /apollo/authored-sets/{set_id}` returns detail, per-problem
`result_summary` (each live problem enriched with capped `problem_text` and the
whitelisted `review` projection — see the enrichment note above), and the
ingestion observability surface (`ingest_run` +
per-page `pages`: `page_ref`, `ocr_text`, `ocr_confidence`,
`verify_path_fired`), and
`POST /apollo/authored-sets/{set_id}/problems/{problem_id}/approve` promotes a
held problem using the teacher-selected OCR or generated reference.
- `apollo.provisioning.validate_pair(question, draft, *, retrieve_fn, judge_fn) -> PairingVerdict{paired, faithful, failed_claims, confidence}` (WU-3B2e stage 3; the §8B two-phase span-grounded pairing/correctness gate). The judge sees the SAME grounding the generator used (`draft.grounding`, else re-grounds via `retrieve_fn`): Phase A pairing (short-circuits Phase B when not paired), Phase B claim-decomposed faithfulness (any unentailed claim → `faithful=False` + `failed_claims`). **FAIL-CLOSED — the EXPLICIT INVERSION of `leakage_judge`'s fail-open:** a malformed/non-JSON/exception/non-object judge response at EITHER phase ⇒ `paired=False, faithful=False, confidence=0.0, failed_claims=("<unparseable judge response>",)` (a REJECT, never an approval); all `judge_fn` calls route through one `_judge_or_fail_closed` helper. `apollo.provisioning.rejection_from_verdict(verdict) -> Rejection | None` is the single fail-mapping point (None on approved; else `Rejection{stage='pairing_gate', reason ∈ unparseable_judge/not_paired/unfaithful_claims, diagnostic, failed_claims}` that 3B2g writes to `apollo_rejected_problems`). Logs ONE `pairing_verdict` line (counts + booleans + `solution_source` ONLY — NO text, NO PII). `judge_fn`/`retrieve_fn` injected (mocked in Tier-1 — NO network, NO DB). This unit hands typed values UP — it does NOT mint (3B2d), promote/lint/write rows (3B2g), or meter/queue (3B2f). Both judge phases now send a SCHEMA-EXPLICIT system prompt (`_PAIRING_PHASE_A_SYSTEM_PROMPT`/`_PAIRING_PHASE_B_SYSTEM_PROMPT`, declaring the exact `paired`/`confidence` and `claims:[{claim,entailed}]` keys) + a strict `response_format` json_schema (`build_pairing_phase_a_schema`/`build_pairing_phase_b_schema`); previously it sent NO system prompt under a JSON `response_format`, so a real model 400'd ("'messages' must contain the word 'json'") and EVERY pair fail-closed to a REJECT. `test_validate_pair_sends_system_prompt_and_json_schema` pins the wiring.
- `apollo.knowledge_graph.resolution_store.write_resolution(neo, attempt_id, result, *, resolved_at) -> ResolutionWriteResult{edges, fields}` (WU-3C2; edges + fields in two idempotent passes) — also `write_resolves_to(neo, attempt_id, specs) -> int` (idempotent `MERGE` of `RESOLVES_TO`; empty → 0 without a session; raises `ResolutionUnavailableError(stage='write_resolves_to')`) and `persist_resolution_fields(neo, attempt_id, specs) -> int` (idempotent `SET`; `stage='persist_fields'` on failure); pure mapping seams `resolved_node_to_edge_spec`/`resolved_node_to_field_spec`.
- `apollo.graph_compare.validate_student_graph(student_graph: KGGraph) -> None` / `validate_reference(problem: dict) -> None` (WU-4A1; the §6.4 step-4 + §6.6 raw-graph gates — return `None` on a valid graph, else raise `StudentGraphInvalidError`/`ReferenceGraphInvalidError` carrying a `reasons` tuple; the reference side delegates to `validate_reference_graph`).
- `apollo.graph_compare.build_student_canonical(student_graph: KGGraph, resolution: ResolutionResult) -> CanonicalGraph` (WU-4A1; S_norm — merge student nodes by resolved key, normalize edges to canonical endpoints, DROP unresolved-endpoint edges (counted in `dropped_edge_count`), RETAIN unresolved nodes as `unresolved_nodes` findings-input; pure + deterministic, takes an ALREADY-computed `ResolutionResult` so the core stays LLM-free). **Phase 0 (resolver safety, 2026-06-23):** (1) the merged `CanonicalNode.node_type` is now computed EXPLICITLY over all member nodes — when members agree (the common path, guaranteed after the resolver type-gate) it is the shared type byte-identically; on a should-never-fire disagreement it is a DETERMINISTIC pick (lowest `node_type` lexicographically — `NodeType` is a `str` `Literal` with NO IntEnum priority — then lowest member id) and `canonical.py`'s new module logger `_LOG` emits a `canonical_merge_type_disagreement` WARNING naming the key + types (the equation symbolic surface still comes from `member_nodes[0]`). (2) A post-merge PRECEDES self-loop — an edge whose endpoints collapse to the same key AFTER merge (`from_key == to_key`), which the parser-layer PRE-merge guard cannot catch — is DROPPED and counted into the existing `dropped_edge_count` (no new field). The logger is the only IO in this otherwise-pure builder; it fires solely on the never-fire branch, so the return-value-equality purity tests are unaffected.
- `apollo.graph_compare.build_reference_canonical(problem: dict) -> ReferenceGraph` (WU-4A1; R_norm — per-problem `reference_solution` nodes; edges are the `depends_on` dependency DAG PLUS the `USES` edges from each procedure step's `uses_equations` and the `PRECEDES` chain over procedure `content.order` (edge-symmetric with `Problem.to_kg_graph` as of 2026-06-22, so `usage`/`edge_coverage` score real structure instead of being vacuously 1.0 / dead by construction); plus one `ReferencePathView` per `declared_paths` entry; validates the reference FIRST (raises `ReferenceGraphInvalidError`); reads the problem's OWN reference_solution, NEVER the deduped entity payload. **G4:** resolves each step's `entry_type` via `_node_type_for_entry` (`variable_mapping` is now a first-class type); a still-unmapped entry_type is DEGRADED — its node + every edge/declared-path slot referencing it are dropped — instead of `KeyError`-ing).
- `apollo.graph_compare.build_problem_candidates(problem: dict, misconceptions: dict, *, canon_key_by_canonical_key: dict[str, int]) -> ProblemInputs` (WU-4A1; assembles the closed candidate set (REUSING `build_candidate_set`/`candidates_from_reference_solution`/`candidates_from_misconceptions`) + assembles the symbolic substitution table via `_collect_symbolic_mappings`: base = the problem-level `symbolic_mappings` key (default `{}`), EXTENDED by each declared `simplification`'s explicit `content.substitution` map (so a student equation in the derived/post-simplification form resolves to the governing equation node); `applies_when` is NEVER parsed. Problem-level keys win on collision (`setdefault`); result is a NEW dict. This is the seam that plumbs the per-problem table into `resolve_attempt(student_graph, inputs.candidates, symbolic_mappings=inputs.symbolic_mappings)` — WU-4A1 does NOT call the resolver itself; the caller/WU-4C does).
- `apollo.graph_compare.grade_attempt(student_canonical: CanonicalGraph, reference_graph: ReferenceGraph) -> GradeResult` (WU-4A2; the §6.4 steps 10/11/13 over PURE inputs — coverage MAX-over-paths, soundness contradictions-only (`misc.` key prefix), the 7 sub-scores, bisimilarity (`harmonic_mean`, `a+b==0 → 0`, never NaN); emits the in-memory §2 `Finding` set (covered/missing-on-winning-path/alternative_path/contradiction/unsupported_extra/unresolved/matched_edge/missing_edge), deterministically ordered; `comparison_confidence == 1.0` in v1. Procedure-order penalizes only true PRECEDES inversions; edges are diagnostic-only (`INFERRED_EDGE_WEIGHT=0.5`, explicit > inferred) and never move the top-line scores; **NO event conversion, NO abstention, NO persistence, NO Neo4j/PG/LLM** — those are WU-4B/WU-4C. The single callable WU-4C wires into `done.py`).
- `compute_coverage(student_graph: KGGraph, reference_graph: KGGraph) -> dict` (async; LLM).
- `compute_rubric(coverage, reference_nodes, *, misconception_scores=None) -> dict` (pure).
- `generate_diagnostic(*, coverage, reference_steps, problem_text, rubric, model=None) -> str` (LLM).
- `draft_reply(history, kg_summary, *, problem_text=None, model=None, history_summary=None, clarification_hints=None) -> str`. When `clarification_hints` (a list of hint strings) is present they are joined and appended as one extra system message (prefixed by `_CLARIFICATION_PREFIX`) that steers Apollo to weave the question(s) naturally into its confused reply without stating the answer; absent → byte-identical to today.
- `Problem.to_kg_graph(attempt_id) -> KGGraph`; `load_problem(path)`; `load_concept(subject_id, concept_id)`.
- `compute_xp_earned(*, overall_score, difficulty, is_reattempt) -> int`; `apply_xp(*, db, user_id, xp_delta)`.

Core types (`apollo/ontology/`):
- **Node types** (Pydantic discriminated union on `node_type`): `equation` (`symbolic`, `label`, `variables`), `condition` (`applies_when`), `simplification` (`applies_when`, `transformation`), `definition` (`concept`, `meaning`), `variable_mapping` (`term`, `symbol`), `procedure_step` (`action`, `purpose`). Common fields: `node_id`, `attempt_id`, `source` (`parser|reference|system`), `parser_confidence` (default 1.0), `status` (`ACCEPTED|DISPUTED|DUAL`), `student_belief` (str|None).
- **Edge types** (`EdgeType` StrEnum) with allowed-pair validation: `PRECEDES` (proc→proc; ordering — there is no `order` int on nodes), `USES` (proc→equation), `DEPENDS_ON` (any→any, no self-loops), `SCOPES` (simplification/condition→equation). Common field `provenance` (`explicit|inferred`, default `explicit`; WU-2A): the parser tags LLM-emitted edges, deterministic-fallback and reference-graph edges keep the `explicit` default. As of WU-2A the parser emits all four edge types (SCOPES and DEPENDS_ON were previously dead / reference-graph-only); cross-turn edges are produced when a `graph_context` is supplied.
- **DEPENDS_ON direction (DAG-0, 2026-07-12)**: KG reference graphs and both canonical graphs use exactly one direction: **prerequisite → dependent**. `Problem.to_kg_graph` and `build_reference_canonical` mint that direction. The parser prompt intentionally retains its linguistic wire convention, **dependent → prerequisite** ("from relies on to"), and `build_student_canonical` flips only parser DEPENDS_ON endpoints at the canonical boundary; no parser prompt was changed. Exact directed edge findings/edge coverage therefore compare the same semantic tuple on both sides. The dependency subscore remains intentionally unordered, and bisimilarity/legacy coverage are node-based. Smart-question planning reverses the canonical adjacency only to build its dependent→prerequisite lookup; misconception centrality counts DEPENDS_ON out-degree. `COMPARISON_VERSION = "graph-compare-v2"` isolates these matching semantics from v1 rows. **Exception:** Postgres Layer-1 `EntityPrereq` rows retain their legacy **dependent → prerequisite** (`from depends on to`) convention; they are not KG/canonical edges and were not migrated by DAG-0. The Neo4j `:Canon` projection is node-only and copies no prerequisite edges.
- **Coverage result**: `{per_step: {ref_id: "covered"|"missing"}, procedure_scores: {ref_id: 0..1}, confidences: {ref_id: 0..1}, negotiation_counts: {dual, disputed, paraphrased, skipped}}`.
- **Rubric result**: `{overall: {score, letter}, procedure|justification|simplification|misconception_corrected: {score, letter, present[, detected, resolved]}}`. Letter bands A+..F (`rubric.LETTER_BANDS`).
- **Done response**: `{rubric, diagnostic_narrative, coverage, transcript: [{role: "student"|"apollo", content, turn_index}], progress: {xp_earned, xp_before/after, level_before/after, level_up, title_after, level_progress_pct, xp_to_next_level}, ...flat legacy XP fields}`. `transcript` is the graded attempt's ordered chat and soft-fails to `[]`. The topic-ledger prompt receives display names, statuses, and whole-number percentages only; every narrative passes through `sanitize_narrative` before serving.
- **Canonical-space types** (`apollo/graph_compare/canonical.py`, WU-4A1; all `@dataclass(frozen=True)`, all collection fields tuples): `CanonicalNode{canonical_key, node_type, source_node_ids, evidence_spans, symbolic=None, method=None, confidence=None}` (one canonical node — for S_norm the merge of all student nodes resolving to `canonical_key` carrying both raw node-ids + per-source evidence spans; for R_norm one reference step with empty evidence and `None` method/confidence); `CanonicalEdge{edge_type, from_key, to_key, provenance}` (a normalized edge whose endpoints are canonical keys); `CanonicalGraph{nodes, edges, unresolved_nodes, dropped_edge_count}` (S_norm — `unresolved_nodes` is a tuple of `(raw node_id, surface_text)` findings-input, `dropped_edge_count` is the count of edges dropped for an unresolved endpoint); `ReferencePathView{canonical_keys}` (one declared acceptable solution path as an ordered key tuple); `ReferenceGraph{nodes, edges, paths}` (R_norm — reference nodes + the `depends_on` DAG + `USES`/`PRECEDES` edges (from procedure `uses_equations` / `content.order`, edge-symmetric with `Problem.to_kg_graph`) + one path view per `declared_paths` entry, `paths` length ≥ 1); `ProblemInputs{candidates, symbolic_mappings}` (`apollo/graph_compare/problem_inputs.py` — the closed candidate set + the per-problem symbolic-mapping table fed to `resolve_attempt`).
- **Grading-result types** (`apollo/graph_compare/core.py` + `findings.py`, WU-4A2; all `@dataclass(frozen=True)`): `GradeResult{coverage_score, soundness_score, bisimilarity_score, node_coverage_score, edge_coverage_score, scoping_score, usage_score, procedure_order_score, dependency_score, contradiction_score, comparison_confidence, findings, soundness_applicable=True, comparison_version}` — the 10 `*_score` fields are named 1:1 to the `apollo_graph_comparison_runs` columns so WU-4B persists with no reshaping; `comparison_confidence` is the score-math's own value (1.0 in v1), the persisted confidence column is `normalization_confidence` (supplied by WU-4B as a type-normalized MIN over resolution method-caps; see the `compute_normalization_confidence` bullet below), so it is carried but NOT persisted by this name; there is intentionally NO `events` field (finding→event conversion is WU-4B §6.5). **D5/D6 empty-bank N/A rule**: `grade_attempt(…, bank_applicable=False)` is called by the orchestrator when `load_for_concept` returns an empty list OR `concept_id` is None — in that case `soundness_score` and `contradiction_score` are `None` (never `1.0`; a `1.0` would be fail-open "verified sound" that was never checked), `bisimilarity_score` is set to `coverage_score` (coverage-only fallback; `bisimilarity.py` detects `soundness is None`), and `soundness_applicable=False` is set on `GradeResult` + persisted to `apollo_graph_comparison_runs.soundness_applicable` (migration 031; column default `true`). The orchestrator (`done_grading.py`) logs the `soundness_not_applicable_empty_bank` warning; coverage grades NORMALLY. **Lane B3a/D1 (2026-07-02):** under the emergent-misconception design an empty `apollo_misconceptions` bank is the NORMAL cold-start state of every class, NOT a reason to abstain. The `misconception_bank_empty` abstention reason string is **REMOVED** — `apply_abstention`/`build_audited_grade` no longer take a `misconception_bank_empty` kwarg and the `REASON_MISCONCEPTION_BANK_EMPTY` constant is gone (interface change: harness abstention histograms no longer see it). The empty-bank fact rides solely on `GradeResult.soundness_applicable=False` and surfaces as an explicit machine-readable marker `misconceptions_status = {"assertable": false, "reason": "empty_bank", "detail": "no misconceptions asserted (empty bank)"}` (`artifact_build.MISCONCEPTIONS_STATUS_KEY`/`MISCONCEPTIONS_STATUS_EMPTY_BANK`). **B3a rework (PR #85):** the marker is **nested inside the artifact's `abstention` JSONB block** (`abstention.misconceptions_status`), the one flexible slot `GradingArtifact` already persists — a top-level payload key has no artifact column and was silently dropped by `artifact_writer._artifact_row` before it reached the row OR the served scorecard. It is emitted on **BOTH grader paths** — `build_graph_artifact` (gated on `shadow.grade.soundness_applicable`) and `build_llm_artifact` (gated on a new `misconceptions_bank_empty` kwarg) — because the LLM fallback is the SERVED (`role='canonical'`) grade whenever the graph grade is not promoted (the default build state), so the marker must exist on the LLM payload for the served scorecard to see it. `write_artifacts` sources that kwarg from `shadow.grade.soundness_applicable` when the shadow ran, else from the SAME source the grading path uses — `candidate_assembly.misconception_bank_applicable(db, concept_id=sess.concept_id)` (isolated `load_for_concept` + the shared `_bank_applicable` predicate, so graph and LLM can never disagree). Both remain **conditional, only on the empty-bank path**, so a seeded-bank artifact's `abstention` block stays byte-identical (no extra key). `render_scorecard` reads `abstention.misconceptions_status` and emits two additional keys — `watch_out_status` (`checked` | `not_checked_empty_bank`) + a teacher-facing `watch_out_note` (cold-start explanation, `None` on the checked path) — so an empty *Watch out* list from a cold-start class (never assessed) is visibly distinct from one that was checked and found none. The `abstained` flag is unchanged in ALL cases (empty bank was already `abstained=False`), so the campaign harness's `shadow_abstained = graph_payload.abstention.abstained` signal is untouched. Persistence (`persistence.py:grade_to_run_spec`) coerces `None` soundness to the coverage fallback value for the `NOT NULL` DB column. **Readers MUST check `soundness_applicable` before averaging or trusting the soundness/bisimilarity columns**. `Finding{kind, canonical_key, student_node_ids, reference_node_ids, evidence_spans, score, confidence, message}` maps onto `apollo_graph_comparison_findings` columns (edge findings key the edge in `message` and leave the id tuples empty — diagnostic only). `FindingKind` (StrEnum) is the §2 finding-kind set and equals `models.FINDING_KINDS` 1:1 (`covered_node, missing_node, matched_edge, missing_edge, unsupported_extra, contradiction, unresolved, alternative_path`; a test asserts the equality). `COMPARISON_VERSION = "graph-compare-v2"` is the single source for the runs row `comparison_version` (a re-run at the same version is a supersede per the UNIQUE constraint). Documented v1 calibration constants: `soundness.CONTRADICTION_UNIT_PENALTY = 0.5`, `scores.INFERRED_EDGE_WEIGHT = 0.5`, `soundness.MISCONCEPTION_KEY_PREFIX = "misc."`.
- **Runs+findings persistence** (`apollo/grading/persistence.py`, WU-4B3): `apollo.grading.persist_comparison_run(db, *, attempt_id, user_id, search_space_id, grade, audited, normalization_confidence, reference_graph_hash) -> run_id` — §6.4 step 15: persists the comparison run + one findings row per `audited.findings` Finding in ONE transaction with **SUPERSEDE** (a re-run at the same `(attempt_id, comparison_version)` DELETEs the prior run → CASCADEs its findings → reinserts; the `UNIQUE` never crashes a legit retry), persists **ALWAYS** (even abstained runs, `abstained=true`), and does NOT `commit()` (the caller WU-4C `done.py` owns the txn boundary). Pure mapping seams `grade_to_run_spec`/`finding_to_row_spec`/`findings_to_row_specs` + the frozen `RunRowSpec`/`FindingRowSpec` value objects (DB-free, 1:1 column mapping; `entity_id` NULL in v1 — the canonical_key→entity-id join is not a WU-4B3 concern; `student_edge_ids`/`reference_edge_ids` always `[]` — edges are message-only). **NUL-byte sanitization (2026-07-02, campaign-harness F1 defect fix):** `finding_to_row_spec` runs `evidence_spans` and `message` through `indexing.text_sanitization.sanitize_jsonable` (the same textbook-NUL-bytes fix, PR #15) before building the spec — a raw `\x00` in a student's typed utterance flows verbatim through parsing into a `Finding`'s quoted evidence text, and Postgres TEXT/JSONB reject `\x00` outright (`asyncpg.exceptions.UntranslatableCharacterError`) at the `apollo_graph_comparison_findings` INSERT, 500-ing `/done` AFTER the student-facing grade had already committed. Node ids are resolver-internal labels (never raw student text) and are left as-is.
- **`apollo.grading.compute_normalization_confidence(audited_grade, resolution, node_type_by_id=None) -> float`** (`normalization_confidence.py`, WU-4B3; G1 type-aware fix 2026-06-26): the §3 damper input — the conservative MIN (weakest-link) over the **type-normalized** per-node method-cap of the resolved nodes backing a SCORED finding (covered/contradiction). Each backing node's raw `ResolvedNode.confidence` (its method-cap) is divided by the MAX confidence its `node_type` can realistically reach (`RESOLUTION_CEILING_BY_TYPE = {"equation": 1.00}`, else `RESOLUTION_CEILING_DEFAULT = 0.75` — the llm tier, the ceiling for conceptual/prose nodes) and clamped to 1.0, BEFORE the MIN. This makes the 0.85 abstention floor (`abstention.py`) judge "resolved within X% of what this node type could achieve" instead of a flat absolute: an equation that fell to llm/fuzzy is suspicious (it had exact/symbolic/derived paths) → abstains; a conceptual node at its llm ceiling is NOT suspicious → does not. Before the fix the floor sat above the only tier prose nodes could reach, so every attempt with procedural content abstained categorically. The `node_id -> node_type` map is threaded from the attempt's student nodes by both callers (`done_grading.py` / `audited_grade.py` build the SAME map from `student_nodes`, keeping the persisted nc byte-identical to the gate's internal value); the optional `None` default keeps the public signature back-compatible and treats unmapped nodes as prose. Returns `NORMALIZATION_CONFIDENCE_FLOOR_WHEN_NO_SCORED_NODES = 1.0` when no scored finding has a resolved backer (a named calibration knob). Feeds `grader_confidence = normalization_confidence × comparison_confidence` (§3 line 431). **§10 composite abstention gate (`APOLLO_ABSTENTION_COMPOSITE`, default OFF; `docs/_archive/design/2026-07-06-abstention-signal-decision-memo.md`):** the memo proved `unresolved_rate`/`normalization_confidence` are VOLUME signals that cannot separate strong attempts from misconception-control attempts (both bands overlap 0.38–0.92). When the flag is ON, `apply_abstention` (`abstention.py`) ignores those two gates for the `abstained` decision and instead grades iff `GradeResult.node_coverage_score >= APOLLO_COMPOSITE_COVERAGE_MIN` (default `0.6`, config/settings.py `apollo_composite_coverage_min`) — a CONTENT signal already reference-denominated (fraction of the problem's expected reference set the resolver credited), independent of how many extra/over-segmented student nodes exist. Coverage below the threshold abstains with the new `REASON_COMPOSITE_LOW_COVERAGE` reason. Detected `CONTRADICTION` findings (misconceptions) are counted (`build_audited_grade`'s `_contradiction_count`) and recorded in the decision's audit trail but do **NOT** force abstention on their own — a detected misconception is informative feedback, not grading uncertainty. The pre-existing volume-gate reasons (`unresolved_rate_above_threshold`, `normalization_confidence_below_threshold`) still get RECORDED when their thresholds trip (informative/auditable) even though they no longer drive `abstained` under the composite. The decision + inputs travel as `Abstention.composite`/`AuditedGrade.composite` (`{coverage, contradictions, coverage_min, decision}`, `None` unless the flag was on for that attempt) and are nested verbatim under the artifact's `abstention.composite` key by `artifact_build.build_graph_artifact` — flag-OFF artifacts carry no such key (byte-identical). `campaign/replay.py`'s `ReplayOutcome.node_coverage` exposes the same `GradeResult.node_coverage_score` signal so an offline threshold sweep can be done from one replay run without re-running the harness per candidate threshold.
- **`apollo.grading.reference_graph_hash(reference_graph) -> str`** (`reference_hash.py`, WU-4B3): a deterministic STABLE sorted-canonical sha256 over the `ReferenceGraph` AS GRADED — nodes (key+type+symbolic) + edges + path key-tuples, order-independent; version-prefixed `REFERENCE_HASH_VERSION = "refhash-v1"`. Stable across replays, changes when the teacher edits the reference (so §2's "old runs stay explainable" holds).
- **§6.11 executable corpus** (`apollo/grading/fixtures/corpus.py`, WU-4B3): 12 adversarial `CorpusFixture` rows + the §6.9 Bernoulli capstone, each shipping expected findings AND events, driving `build_audited_grade → convert_findings_to_events` (deterministic resolution + injected `audit_fn`, no live LLM); the persistence-touching rows (parser-miss, high-unresolved, Bernoulli) run on REAL PG.
- **Graph-sim candidate-grade types** (`apollo/grading/`, WU-4C2; all `@dataclass(frozen=True)`): `RubricRefNode{node_id, node_type}` (the duck-typed reference-node `compute_rubric` reads — `node_id` carries the graph-sim `canonical_key`) + `RubricMappingInput{coverage, reference_nodes, misconception_scores}` (the exact `compute_rubric` bag) from `apollo.grading.findings_to_rubric_input(*, audited, reference_graph, opposes_map, turn_order) -> RubricMappingInput` / `build_graph_sim_rubric(*, ...) -> dict` (`rubric_mapping.py`). `AxisDelta{axis, old_score, shadow_score, delta}` (`None` on an absent side) + `CalibrationMetrics{letter_agreement, old_overall_letter, shadow_overall_letter, overall_score_delta, axis_deltas, divergent, comparison_version}` from `apollo.grading.compute_calibration_metrics(*, old_rubric, shadow_rubric) -> CalibrationMetrics` (`calibration.py`, §6.7); constants `CALIBRATION_VERSION = "calibration-v1"`, `DIVERGENCE_SCORE_THRESHOLD = 10` (the human-review trip wire). `DiagnosticFinding{kind, canonical_key, evidence_spans, message}` + `DiagnosticRequest{findings, covered_keys, missing_keys, misconception_keys}` (NO `transcript` field — findings-only §6.8) + `ConstrainedDiagnostic{narrative, used_fallback, regenerated, post_check_failures}` from `apollo.grading.generate_constrained_diagnostic(audited, *, llm=None) -> ConstrainedDiagnostic` (`diagnostic.py`, §6.8; `llm` defaults to `main_chat_diagnostic_llm`, a lazily-OpenAI-importing live default; tests inject a deterministic stub). All three carried on the extended `ShadowGradeResult` (`graph_sim_rubric`/`calibration`/`diagnostic`). **G4:** `ShadowGradeResult` also carries an OPTIONAL `degradation: GraphSimDegradation | None` (default `None`) — non-None only when a minted payload carried a reference entry_type the graph-sim node-type map could not consume (those steps were dropped, never a KeyError); it names the offending types so paired analysis sees the simulation was partial.

## Main data flows

**Neo4j degraded mode (2026-07-11):** every flow below assumes a healthy
Neo4j driver and is BYTE-IDENTICAL when it is. When Neo4j is down (missing
env, Aura unreachable, a connection dying mid-request), each flow's KG
step(s) degrade per the "Neo4j degraded-mode carve-out" bullet under
Non-obvious conventions — read that once rather than re-deriving it per
flow; the notes below only call out where a flow's degraded behavior is
non-obvious.

**(a) Student teaching turn — `POST /sessions/{id}/chat` (`handlers/chat.py`)**
1. Load session + latest `ProblemAttempt` for `session.current_problem_id`; resolve the concept via `curriculum_db.load_concept_definition(db, concept_id=sess.concept_id)` (DB, course-scoped through the `concept_id` FK).
2. Intent state machine (checklist item #5): if `sess.pending_intent == "done"`, treat the message as a confirmation (`detect_confirmation` regex). Affirmed → dispatch `handle_done` inline and return a chat-shaped envelope with `intent_executed`; rejected/ambiguous → clear pending, fall through. Otherwise classify intent (`classify_intent`, cheap LLM); a non-teaching intent at confidence ≥ 0.7 sets `pending_intent` and returns a confirmation prompt without parsing.
3. Build cross-turn context then parse: chat reads the CURRENT subgraph (`store.read_graph` — the new turn's nodes aren't written yet, so it IS the prior-turns graph) and `build_graph_context` projects it into a `GraphContext` threaded into `parse_utterance` (ONE strict-json_schema GPT-4o call, temp 0.0) → typed nodes (`node_id = "stu_" + uuid12`) + all four typed edges (provenance-tagged), now cross-turn live (WU-2B). The deterministic USES (from `uses_equation_ordinals`, resolved through the ORIGINAL-entry-index map) + PRECEDES (consecutive procedure steps) derivation remains the no-context fallback used when the model emits no edges.
4. Write nodes then edges via `KGStore` (edges MUST be written after nodes — endpoints must exist at CREATE time). `write_nodes` de-dups cross-turn re-assertions by id (a prior id is reused, not cloned). `write_edges` no longer relies on Neo4j silent-drop: it validates endpoint existence + EDGE_ALLOWED_PAIRS BEFORE the CREATE and logs any drop/invalid (`write_edge_rejected` + a `write_edges` summary). Writes are rejected with `SessionFrozenError` if phase ∈ {PROBLEM_REVEAL, SOLVING, REPORT}.
5. Reply: `load_windowed_history` (last 12 turns raw + rolling cheap-LLM summary refreshed every 8 older turns, persisted on `apollo_sessions.history_summary`) → `summarize_for_apollo` (bullet list of the KG) → **clarification loop** (before `draft_reply`, gated by `APOLLO_CLARIFICATION_ENABLED` env flag; default OFF everywhere): when ON, `_find_problem_payload` → `load_problem_candidates` (delegates to the single shared recipe `load_problem_candidates_with_soundness` in `candidate_assembly.py`) assembles the closed candidate set identical to the grading path by construction; before detecting new ones, `resolve_pending_clarifications` (`apollo/clarification/resolve_turn.py`) re-scores the student's current message against any `asked_waiting` rows from prior turns — `rescore_clarification` → `record_outcome` writes `confirmed`/`refuted`/`vague` (+ `clarification_text` = the student message); fail-safe: a judge failure leaves the row `asked_waiting`, never credit on failure; then `run_clarification_detection` (`apollo/clarification/turn.py`) — which early-exits with `[]` when `find_residual_nodes` returns empty (all nodes resolve, no embedding call) — finds residual nodes whose embeddings are ambiguously close to a candidate (cosine ≥ T_AMBIG=0.50), persists `asked_waiting` rows (`write_asked_waiting`), and returns answer-blind probe hint strings; the ENTIRE clarification block is wrapped in a **SAVEPOINT** (`db.begin_nested()`) so a DB fault inside rolls back only the clarification writes and leaves the outer transaction (message-pair commit at the end of the turn) clean — the outer `except` catches any exception, logs a warning, and returns `[]`, never blocking the turn → `draft_reply` with ONLY the problem text + KG summary + history + `clarification_hints` (woven naturally into Apollo's confused reply when present) → **leakage backstop** (when probes were used): `guard_clarification_reply` (`apollo/clarification/leak_guard.py`) runs the leakage judge over the drafted reply; if it CONFIDENTLY detects an answer leak (confidence ≥ `CONFIDENCE_THRESHOLD` 0.6), the reply is re-drafted WITHOUT the probes via the `regenerate_without_probes` lambda; soft-fail-open — a judge error leaves the reply unchanged so teaching is never blocked; uses the judge callable directly, NOT the raising `validate_or_raise`. v1: no sufficiency / misconception / OLM-invite signals and no output filter on this path.
6. Persist the (student, apollo) message pair in one commit; return reply + full KG dump.

**(b) "I'm done teaching" — `POST /sessions/{id}/done` (`handlers/done.py`)**
1. Read the per-attempt graph BEFORE freezing. If `APOLLO_DONE_GATE_ENABLED` (default off): flag parser-sourced entries with `status == DISPUTED` or `parser_confidence < 0.6` that have no row in `apollo_kg_negotiations` → raise `ReviewRequiredError` (422, FE renders a review modal).
2. `store.freeze(session_id)` (phase → PROBLEM_REVEAL), then phase → SOLVING.
3. Reference graph: `problem.to_kg_graph(attempt_id)` from the `reference_solution` carried in `apollo_concept_problems.payload` (DB; resolved via `_find_problem(db, sess.concept_id, sess.current_problem_id)`, NOT `problems/problem_*.json`) — this is the v1 truth source (no retrieval/RAG).
4. `compute_coverage`: all matcher calls run concurrently (`asyncio.to_thread` + `gather`, no `return_exceptions`). Binary types (equation/condition/simplification) are batched one LLM call per type; procedure steps get one partial-credit call each (score ≥ 0.5 → "covered"). DUAL nodes with `student_belief` are graded against the student's wording. Transient failures retry 3x with backoff then raise `CoverageGradingError` (503 — grading unavailable, never a silent downgrade).
5. `compute_rubric` (pure): procedure 0.57 / justification 0.2375 / simplification 0.1425 / misconception_corrected 0.05; absent axes redistribute weight proportionally (no misconceptions → exact pre-P2.8 60/25/15). Misconception scores are read from `apollo_messages.metadata` — since the v1 chat path no longer writes per-turn metadata, this axis is normally absent.
5a. **Parallel misconception-detection stage (T13, `apollo.overseer.misconception_detector`), gated by `APOLLO_MISCONCEPTION_DETECTOR` (default OFF everywhere — with the flag off `handle_done` is byte-identical to pre-T13).** Runs after the rubric (so it can dock its LIVE score) and before the diagnostic (so the narrative reflects the penalized band): `_student_utterances` loads this attempt's `Message.role == "student"` rows → `detect_misconceptions` (parallel `sympy_veto` + `bank_pattern` + `judge_concepts` tiers, DI'd judge/embed fns) → `gate_findings` (REDESIGNED 2026-07-08, A9-A13: `sympy_veto` self-docks; a judge finding bank-keyed via a validated `misconception_code` (A11) that co-keys with ANY `bank_pattern` finding sharing that `bank_code` — floor-free, cross-namespace via a `bank_by_code` index, A10/A13 — docks under the judge, ceiling-eligible; a lone bank-keyed judge clearing `TAU_SOLO_JUDGE` docks penalty-only, never ceiling-eligible, A9/A12; a lone unkeyed or sub-solo-τ judge routes to `needs_clarification`) → `merge_detections` (severity-weighted subtract + ceiling, keyed on `compute_centrality(reference_graph)`) → `rubric_overall_after_penalty(rubric, outcome)` REASSIGNS `rubric` to a NEW dict (never a mutation) whose `overall.score`/`overall.letter` are reduced/recomputed via `score_to_letter` (A4). The resulting `MergeOutcome` (`detection_outcome`) flows into `xp_earned`, `generate_diagnostic`, `student_response["rubric"]`, and `attempt.diagnostic_report` — moving the real band + XP a student sees — and is threaded into `write_artifacts` (T12) below so `build_llm_artifact`'s `misconception_penalty`/`misconceptions[]`/composite (T11) are populated and the emergent ledger feed (T14, gated separately on `APOLLO_EMERGENT_MISCONCEPTIONS`) picks the docked findings up. **SOFT-FAIL (never breaks grading):** the entire detect→gate→merge chain is wrapped in one `try/except Exception` — any failure logs `misconception_detector_failed` and leaves `detection_outcome=None`, so the grade proceeds with the UNPENALIZED rubric and HTTP 200 always. This stage is independent of the D4 coverage fix below (both share the `detector_enabled()` flag but neither depends on the other's code path). **Phase-1 diagnostic trace (2026-07-09, SEPARATE flag `APOLLO_MISC_TRACE`, default OFF):** when ON, after `merge_detections`/`rubric_overall_after_penalty` this block calls `trace.trace_attempt(...)` inside its OWN nested try/except (so a trace defect can never perturb the already-computed grade) to append one JSONL row per reference-graph node revealing the judge verdict + gate row + bank top-1 per node — instrumentation only, no tau/threshold/scoring change; flag OFF ⇒ `trace.py` is never imported and this step is byte-identical. **F-struct structural co-key (2026-07-09, SEPARATE sub-flag `APOLLO_MISC_STRUCT_COKEY`, `struct_cokey_enabled()`, default OFF):** inserted between `detect_misconceptions` and `gate_findings` — sub-flag OFF -> `opposes_index = {}` (the byte-identical default `gate_findings`/`trace_attempt` already had); sub-flag ON -> `_load_bank_entries` (soft-failing local mirror of `detector._load_bank`) loads the concept's misconception bank and `opposes_index.build_opposes_index(reference_graph, bank_entries)` resolves each entry's `opposes` (an `entity_key`) against the reference graph's node `entity_key`s into a `node_id -> bank_code` map, passed to both `gate_findings(..., opposes_index=opposes_index)` and (trace-flag ON) `trace_attempt(..., opposes_index=opposes_index)`. This lets `gate_findings` dock a judge finding that LOCALIZED an error to a node but named no bank code, when the CURRICULUM's own `opposes` authoring already names the opposing misconception for that node — see the `apollo/overseer/` module-map row above for the full gate-branch/schema description. **Opposes seeding is course-scoped:** `scripts/seed_apollo_misconceptions` writes `opposes` per `(search_space_id, concept_id)` row and has no `--source-subject-slug` override (unlike `seed_apollo_learner_model`), so a cloned course (a new `search_space_id` sharing a subject's concepts) does not inherit the original course's `opposes` links — it needs its own seed run before the structural co-key path can fire for it (live-validated 2026-07-09, `docs/_archive/experiments/2026-07-09-apollo-misc-struct-cokey-validation.md`).
6. `generate_diagnostic` (LLM) narrates the rubric verdict — hard-ruled not to contradict per-axis scores, formative tone.
7. Re-attempt detection (`attempt.result` already set, or `has_prior_graded_attempt` cross-session) → `compute_xp_earned` (score × difficulty multiplier 1.0/1.5/2.0 × 0.25 if re-attempt) → `apply_xp` updates `apollo_student_progress` and computes level (5 tiers, thresholds 0/300/800/1600/3000). Attempt gets `result="graded"`, `solver_trace=None`, `diagnostic_report={narrative, rubric, coverage}`; phase → REPORT. The `result` allowlist (`models.ATTEMPT_RESULTS`, enforced by the DB CHECK from migration 009+025: `solved/stuck/skipped/returned_to_hoot/abandoned/graded`) must include every value handlers write — `done.py` writes `graded`, `next.py` writes `abandoned` on a mid-problem switch. `has_prior_graded_attempt` counts `GRADED_ATTEMPT_RESULTS` (all of them except `abandoned`, which is a switch, not a grade).
8. **Retention + Layer-3 (post-commit, NO-FALLBACK).** `done.py` captures ONE `done_ts = datetime.now(UTC)` and calls `store.stamp_graded_at(attempt_id, ts=done_ts)` (Neo4j `graded_at`; `stamp_graded_at` now accepts an optional `ts` — a `datetime` is `.isoformat()`'d, a string passes through, `None` falls back to `now()` — so Neo4j `graded_at` and Postgres `last_evidence_at` carry the IDENTICAL instant). Then, behind `APOLLO_GRAPH_SIM_SHADOW_ENABLED`, the §6.4 shadow graph-simulation chain (WU-4C1/4C2) persists the comparison run + findings. **WU-5A2 step 16/17 (`APOLLO_GRAPH_SIM_LAYER3_ENABLED`, default OFF EVERYWHERE — DORMANT):** when ON, AFTER the shadow persist the Done txn appends `apollo_mastery_events` + upserts `apollo_learner_state` (the §3 Bayesian belief) in ONE all-or-nothing Postgres transaction — `convert_findings_to_events` runs HERE (step 16), each event's `canonical_key` joins to `apollo_kg_entities.id` (unmapped → skipped, never a NULL FK), the recompute base is read from the EVENT LOG (not the self-mutated state row), and `run_learner_update` owns the single commit. A Layer-3 failure sets `attempt.learner_update_pending` (drained by the WU-5B janitor) WITHOUT voiding the already-committed grade. When the flag is OFF (the only build state), the gated call never fires and the Done return + DB side-effects are byte-identical to WU-4C2. **WU-5B3a-0** extracts the shadow-input assembly into `done_inputs.build_rerun_inputs` (shared with the future retry janitor); `done.py` now sources the shadow `problem_payload` through it (keyed on `attempt.problem_id`, the durable per-attempt key), behavior-preserving with all flags OFF — `student_graph`/`old_rubric` stay the LIVE values, only `problem_payload` flows through the builder.

**GEN-5 per-item mastery linkage (2026-07-12).** Migration 045 adds nullable `apollo_mastery_events.concept_problem_id` as the future difficulty-calibration key. Both mutually exclusive mastery writers resolve it at write time through `persistence.problem_linkage`: the Bayesian learner-model path uses the already-scoped session concept plus `attempt.problem_id` once per update, while the composite artifact projection recovers `(concept_id, problem_code)` with one attempt→session join. Resolution prefers a live tier-2 row and returns `None` on a miss, so legacy attempts still append the exact same events with a NULL link; superseded Bayesian replacement rows are resolved and stamped again.

**(c) Hoot handoff — `POST /sessions/from_hoot` (`hoot_bridge/session_init.py`)**
Bearer token → `require_user` resolves `user_id`; `require_course_member` checks membership for the given `search_space_id`. `curriculum_db.list_course_concepts(db, search_space_id)` builds the course's candidate concepts — only those with a TEACHABLE problem (a correlated `EXISTS` on `tier==2 AND quarantined_at IS NULL`, the SAME predicate `list_problems_for_concept` applies, so an empty / tier-1-only / fully-quarantined decoy concept can't be inferred and then crash `select_problem` with `PoolExhaustedError`; the G6 fluids-grading fix) → `infer_concept_id` (GPT-4o, must return one of those candidate `concept_id`s or 409 `no_matching_concept`; a course with no teachable curriculum → empty candidates → null → 409) → `select_problem(db, concept_id, difficulty)` (DB; deterministic: sorted by `Problem.id`, unattempted at difficulty, else `PoolExhaustedError`) → end stale active sessions → create `ApolloSession` (phase TEACHING, `user_id`, `search_space_id`, `concept_id` populated — `concept_cluster_id` no longer written) + `ProblemAttempt` → return `{session_id, attempt_id, problem}`.

## Key dependencies

- **OpenAI** (`openai` sync client, constructed per call): models resolved per call site — parser/coverage/diagnostic/concept-inference use `MAIN_MODEL` (default `gpt-4o`); `draft_reply` uses `APOLLO_MODEL` > `MAIN_MODEL` > `gpt-4o`; cross-checks (intent, triviality, history summarizer, leakage judge) use `APOLLO_CHEAP_MODEL` (default `gpt-4o-mini`) via `agent/_llm.cheap_chat`. Every `_llm` call logs `{event: "llm_call", purpose, model, tokens}` for cost audit.
- **Neo4j** (`neo4j` async driver) — **OPTIONAL at runtime (degraded mode, 2026-07-11).** `Neo4jClient.from_env()` requires `NEO4J_URI`, `NEO4J_USERNAME`, `NEO4J_PASSWORD`, `NEO4J_DATABASE` (Aura instance — see project memory). One driver per process, lazily built in `api.py`; `close_neo4j_client()` should be wired to app shutdown. `get_neo4j_client()` returns `Neo4jClient | None` — a construction failure (missing/bad env, Aura unreachable) is logged (`apollo_neo4j_client_construction_failed`) and degrades to `None` rather than raising; NO NEGATIVE CACHING, so the next request retries construction fresh. This is safe because the served grade is the transcript LLM grader (`APOLLO_TRANSCRIPT_GRADER=1`) — the Neo4j graph lane is shadow-only — so chat/done/session-lifecycle survive Neo4j being down entirely. Every route handler param widened to `Neo4jClient | None`; `KGStore.__init__` accepts the same and every Neo4j-backed method guards via `self._require_neo(stage=...)`, raising `KGUnavailableError` at entry when `neo is None` (Postgres-only `KGStore` methods — freeze/unfreeze/get_node_trace — are unaffected). The KG-native negotiation routes (`negotiate.py`) and `restart_problem` wrap their store calls in `KG_DEGRADED_ERRORS` (`apollo/persistence/neo4j_client.py`: `KGUnavailableError`, `DriverError`, `AuthError`, `TransientError`, `DatabaseUnavailable`, `OSError`, `asyncio.TimeoutError` — Neo4j missing/unreachable/broken-connection, deliberately NOT Cypher/data errors) and re-raise as `KGUnavailableError` → the new `kg_unavailable` 503 handler. Teacher-facing authored-set provisioning (`provisioning/authored_sets/api.py`) is Neo4j-native with no meaningful degraded path, so it routes every `get_neo4j_client()` call through a local `_require_neo` guard (mirrors `apollo.api.require_neo4j_client`, kept as a separate sync helper because the authored-sets call sites are plain function calls / a background task, not FastAPI `Depends` resolution) → the same 503. See "NO FALLBACK policy" below for the exact degraded-mode behavior per route/stage.
- **SymPy**: `solver/sympy_exec.py` (zero-form parsing, `solve_system`) — in v1 only the LaTeX display path in `store.py` exercises it at runtime.
- **Authentication**: all routes require Supabase bearer auth via `auth.py` primitives (`resolve_auth_context`, run off the event loop). `apollo/auth_deps.py` provides four gate functions: `require_user` (bare auth, used by `from_hoot` and `progress`), `require_course_member` (membership check at session creation), `require_course_teacher` (role='teacher' membership check, no auto-enroll fallback — gates the authored-sets endpoints), and `require_session_owner` (FastAPI Depends gate on session-scoped routes — 401/403/404 as appropriate). Identity never comes from the request body.
- **Supabase Postgres tables** (via the repo-wide async SQLAlchemy `database.session.get_db_session`): `apollo_sessions` (`user_id UUID`, `search_space_id`, migration 023; `concept_id` FK into `apollo_concepts` (018) is now POPULATED at session creation, and the legacy `concept_cluster_id` TEXT column was DROPPED in migration 027 / WU-3D), `apollo_messages` (JSONB `metadata`, migration 020), `apollo_problem_attempts`, `apollo_student_progress` (`user_id UUID`, migration 023), `apollo_kg_negotiations` (migration 021), plus the DB-curriculum tables `apollo_subjects`/`apollo_concepts`/`apollo_concept_problems` (018) and `apollo_misconceptions` (019, vector(3072) embeddings). Partial unique index `ix_apollo_sessions_unique_active_per_user` enforces one active session per user. **Migration 028 (WU-5B3a-0, next on-disk after 027)** adds the five `apollo_problem_attempts.learner_update_*` dead-letter/backoff columns + the partial index `apollo_problem_attempts_pending_idx` (DDL + ORM only; the WU-5B3a-1 `learner_janitor.drain_pending_attempts` claim/recompute/record state machine is the consumer). NOT applied to any remote DB by an agent — deploy is a human/CI step (test rehearsal, then prod). **Migration 037 (lane B3b/D1)** adds `apollo_misconception_observations` — the emergent-store append-only observation ledger (`search_space_id` CASCADE / `concept_id` SET NULL / `attempt_id` SET NULL, `UNIQUE(attempt_id, signature)` idempotency, RLS-stopgap default-deny, index `ix_apollo_misconception_obs_space_concept`). 036 is claimed by a sibling lane's PR, so this store took 037. Same deploy discipline: agents apply to LOCAL Docker Postgres only.
- **tiktoken** (best-effort): token estimate for `draft_reply`'s 100k budget; falls back to chars/4.
- **Env flags**: `APOLLO_DONE_GATE_ENABLED` (off), `APOLLO_OLM_INVITES_ENABLED` (off). **WU-5B3b** adds `APOLLO_LEARNER_JANITOR_ENABLED` (off EVERYWHERE — gates the dormant `apollo-janitor` worker's per-pass drain; flipping it ON is a HUMAN deploy decision, and `APOLLO_GRAPH_SIM_LAYER3_ENABLED` must ALSO be ON for the drain to write beliefs rather than defer) + the two worker tunables `APOLLO_JANITOR_SWEEP_LIMIT` (1) / `APOLLO_JANITOR_POLL_SECONDS` (60). **WU-6A3** adds `APOLLO_SESSION_PERSONALIZATION_ENABLED` (off EVERYWHERE — gates the session-personalization wedge at BOTH selection call-sites, `hoot_bridge/session_init.py` (session start) + `handlers/next.py` (advance), via `overseer.select_problem_personalized`; flag-OFF is byte-identical to the old `select_problem`. **Double-gated:** even flag-ON is a total no-op until `APOLLO_GRAPH_SIM_LAYER3_ENABLED` is ON and `apollo_learner_state` is populated — empty → cold-start `candidates[0]`. Flipping it is a HUMAN deploy decision; behind it the student gets a personalized problem *order* with no UI affordance yet — a known additive student-ui follow-up). **Lane B3b/D1** adds `APOLLO_EMERGENT_MISCONCEPTIONS` (default OFF EVERYWHERE — gates the emergent per-class misconception store at BOTH seams, `handlers/artifact_writer.py` (write) + `clarification/candidate_assembly.py` (read); flag-OFF is byte-identical to hand-authored-bank-only and writes zero ledger rows) plus the PRE-CALIBRATION trust tunables `APOLLO_EMERGENT_K` (3) / `APOLLO_EMERGENT_TAU_ASSERT` (0.5) / `APOLLO_EMERGENT_TAU_PROJECT` (0.2) / `APOLLO_EMERGENT_RECENCY_HALFLIFE_DAYS` (30). **T1–T17 (2026-07-08) adds `APOLLO_MISCONCEPTION_DETECTOR`** (default OFF EVERYWHERE — `apollo.overseer.misconception_detector.config.detector_enabled()`; gates BOTH the T13 parallel detection stage in `done.py` AND the T10 D4 sign/direction prompt+SymPy pre-gate fix in `overseer/coverage.py`; flag-OFF is byte-identical to pre-T1 on every path) plus its calibration constants `TAU_FIRE` (0.85, token-prob path), `TAU_FIRE_VERBALIZED` (0.90, verbalized-confidence fallback path — selected by whether the judge's `verdict_token_prob` is `None`, A1), `SEVERITY_CLAMP`, and `BANK_SIM_FLOOR` (now scoped to standalone `bank_pattern` firing only — corroboration is floor-free, A10/L4). **2026-07-08 corroboration/keying redesign (A9-A13) adds `TAU_SOLO_JUDGE`** (0.90, `APOLLO_MISC_TAU_SOLO_JUDGE` — the stricter bar, ON TOP of the routed τ, that a LONE bank-keyed judge finding must clear to dock on its own; deliberately >= `TAU_FIRE` so a solo dock is strictly harder than a corroborated one). **Independent of, but complementary to, `APOLLO_EMERGENT_MISCONCEPTIONS`:** the detector flag controls whether a misconception is DETECTED AND PENALIZED on the LIVE grade at all; the emergent flag controls whether a detected/docked finding is ALSO written to the emergent per-class ledger (`apollo_misconception_observations`, migration 037) for future promotion. Both OFF (today's only prod state) → no detection, no penalty, no ledger row. Detector ON + emergent OFF → findings dock the rubric/composite but never reach the ledger. Detector ON + emergent ON (T14's tested combination) → docked findings both penalize the grade and feed the emergent store. Emergent ON + detector OFF is a no-op for this stage (nothing is ever detected to feed it) — the two flags are AND'd at the ledger-feed seam, never a substitute for one another. Flipping the flag ON is a HUMAN deploy decision gated on calibrating those constants against a real corpus. **Phase-1 (2026-07-09) adds `APOLLO_MISC_TRACE`** (default OFF EVERYWHERE — `config.trace_enabled()`; a SEPARATE flag from `APOLLO_MISCONCEPTION_DETECTOR`, so a diagnostic trace can be switched on without changing whether the penalty applies) plus `APOLLO_MISC_TRACE_PATH` (default `campaign/out/misconception_trace.jsonl`). Instrumentation ONLY (no tau/gate/threshold/scoring change): a machine-parseable per-node JSONL trace of the judge verdict + gate row + bank top-1, for diagnosing the recall gap (why some misconception attempts still band Strong). Flag OFF ⇒ byte-identical. Phase 2 (planned, spec `docs/_archive/specs/2026-07-09-apollo-misconception-trace-and-tau-calibration-design.md`) is the log-first data-driven tau / co-key-relaxation calibration, HARD-constrained to keep control false-positives 0/4. **F-struct (2026-07-09) adds `APOLLO_MISC_STRUCT_COKEY`** (default OFF EVERYWHERE — `config.py::struct_cokey_enabled()`; a SEPARATE sub-flag from `APOLLO_MISCONCEPTION_DETECTOR`, meaningful only when the detector flag is also ON). Gates whether `done.py` builds a real `opposes_index` (`node_id -> bank_code`, resolved from the reference graph's node `entity_key`s against the misconception bank's `opposes` column, migration 039) and threads it into `gate_findings`/`trace_attempt`, letting a judge finding that localizes an error to a node WITHOUT naming a validated code still dock when the curriculum's own authored `opposes` link names the misconception — spec `docs/_archive/specs/2026-07-09-apollo-misconception-struct-cokey-design.md`. Flag OFF (today's only state everywhere) ⇒ `opposes_index` stays `{}` and `build_opposes_index`/`opposes_index.py` is never even imported — byte-identical to pre-F-struct behavior. Flipping it ON is a HUMAN deploy decision gated on the same recall-vs-false-positive calibration Phase 2 above targets.

## Non-obvious conventions

- **NO FALLBACK policy**: every failure mode is a named exception in `apollo/errors.py` with its own HTTP status + `error_code` registered in `api.py` (`register_exception_handlers`). Never soft-fail a grade or silently truncate context. Exceptions: deliberately soft-failing helpers — triviality classifier (→ trivial), intent classifier (→ "teaching"), history summarizer (→ no summary), LaTeX render (→ None). **WU-3C1 adds two named errors that are deliberately NOT registered as HTTP handlers in this unit** (api.py is out of WU-3C1 scope; both surface on non-request / post-grade paths): `CanonProjectionError(stage, last_error)` — raised by the `:Canon` seeder (`load_entities`/`merge_canon`), surfaced via the operational CLI's non-zero exit, never leaving a partial authoritative `:Canon` graph; and `RetentionError(attempt_id, last_error)` — raised by `stamp_graded_at`, which runs AFTER the grade/XP commit, so a failure surfaces (loud, never swallowed; a raw 500 if it ever reaches a request) WITHOUT voiding the durable grade — the next Done/retry/janitor re-stamps idempotently. **WU-3C2 adds two more named errors, also deliberately NOT registered as HTTP handlers here** (api.py is out of WU-3C2 scope; WU-4A wires the Done route that triggers resolution and registers both): `ResolutionUnavailableError(stage, last_error)` — resolver INFRASTRUCTURE failure (`stage ∈ {llm_adjudication, write_resolves_to, persist_fields}`), raised when the one LLM adjudication call or a Neo4j `RESOLVES_TO`/field write fails; like `RetentionError` it runs AFTER the grade commits, so it surfaces loud but must NOT void the grade — the caller sets `learner_update_pending=true` and the next Done/janitor retry re-runs the idempotent resolution; the offline drain that CLEARS `learner_update_pending` (set by these `done_grading`/`learner_update` NO-FALLBACK forks) is `learner_janitor.drain_pending_attempts` (WU-5B3a-1) — and the two clocks are DISTINCT: the claim/backoff schedule uses wall-clock `now()` (SQL), the belief Δt anchor uses the FROZEN Neo4j `graded_at` `done_ts` (never `now()`); and `ResolutionInvalidOutputError(returned_key, allowed_keys)` — the HARD case where the one LLM adjudication call returns a key NOT in the closed candidate set (a hallucination); the resolver never fabricates a target. A per-node non-match is NOT an error — it is `unresolved` DATA (no edge, no event, logged; the unresolved rate is a parser-recall / curriculum-gap metric). **WU-3D adds one more internal named error, also NOT HTTP-registered** (matching the WU-3C1/3C2 precedent): `ConceptNotFoundError` (in `subjects/curriculum_db.py`) — raised by `load_concept_definition` when a session's `concept_id` points at a deleted `apollo_concepts` row (a should-never-happen given the `ON DELETE RESTRICT` FK), so it surfaces loudly (raw 500 if it ever reaches a request) rather than silently picking a default concept. **WU-4A1 adds two more, also deliberately NOT HTTP-registered here** (the Done route that triggers grading is WU-4C, which registers them): `StudentGraphInvalidError(reasons: tuple[str, ...])` — the §6.4 step-4 gate (`validate_student_graph`) fails on a raw-student grammar violation (illegal edge endpoints re-derived from node types, a missing endpoint, mixed `attempt_id`, or a PRECEDES cycle); and `ReferenceGraphInvalidError(reasons: tuple[str, ...])` — the §6.6 gate (`validate_reference` / `build_reference_canonical`) fails because the reference graph fails the §6.1 contract (`validate_reference_graph(...).errors` carried verbatim), which blocks grading. Both carry a structured `reasons` tuple and are raised loudly, never swallowed. The two user-facing 409s on the from_hoot path are unchanged: `NoMatchingConceptError` (now raised by `infer_concept_id` on null/unknown/invalid-JSON, including the empty-candidates "course has no curriculum" path) and `PoolExhaustedError` (its `concept_cluster_id` constructor/JSON field is RETAINED for API back-compat — now passed `str(concept_id)`).
- **Neo4j degraded-mode carve-out (2026-07-11, `fix/apollo-neo4j-degraded`)**: distinct from the NO FALLBACK family above — this is infrastructure OPTIONALITY, not a grading bug, so it degrades gracefully rather than raising loud everywhere. `KGUnavailableError(stage, last_error)` is the new named error for "Neo4j missing / unreachable / mid-call driver failure"; `KG_DEGRADED_ERRORS` (`apollo/persistence/neo4j_client.py`) is the shared tuple every call site catches. Per-surface behavior: **chat** — KG reads degrade to an empty `KGGraph`/the store's `_EMPTY_SUMMARY` constant; writes are skipped (`kg_entries_added=0`); the conversational reply (Postgres + OpenAI) ALWAYS proceeds. **done** — the pre-freeze `read_graph` degrades to an empty graph + `kg_degraded=True`; the Done-gate (`APOLLO_DONE_GATE_ENABLED`) is SKIPPED (fail-open) when degraded; if `kg_degraded` AND the transcript grader is off/failed, `handle_done` raises `CoverageGradingError(stage="kg_unavailable_fallback")` INSTEAD of calling `compute_coverage` on the empty graph (grading an empty student graph would silently produce a false F — the existing `coverage_grading_handler` 503 is the correct "try again" signal, not a fabricated zero); the shadow chain (`APOLLO_GRAPH_SIM_SHADOW_ENABLED`) skips entirely when `kg_degraded or neo is None`, stamping `graph_failure="shadow_failure: neo4j_unavailable"` on the canonical artifact (mid-chain Neo4j errors were ALREADY isolated by the existing broad `except Exception` — no change there). **`stamp_graded_at` gets a genuine RELAXATION of the NO-FALLBACK contract**: `handle_done` now catches `(KGUnavailableError, RetentionError)` UNCONDITIONALLY (not gated on `kg_degraded` — the real failure mode is a connection dying DURING the ~4-minute grading pipeline, so a healthy pre-freeze read does not guarantee a healthy stamp), logs a warning, and continues — `RetentionError` has NO registered HTTP handler today, so letting it propagate 500s an already-committed, fully graded Done. **get_session** — the KG read degrades to `{"nodes": [], "edges": []}` (the same literal the pre-existing no-attempt else-branch already returns); `handle_end` is unaffected (its `neo` param was already unused — no Neo4j write happens at end-of-session). **restart_problem** — deliberately does NOT silently skip: the wipe targets the SAME `attempt_id` (no new `ProblemAttempt` row), so a skipped `delete_subgraph` would resurface stale KG nodes once Neo4j returns; degradation raises `KGUnavailableError` (structured 503) instead, and the ordering guarantee (`delete_subgraph` runs BEFORE the Postgres `Message` delete) means nothing is ever half-wiped. **negotiate** (`challenge`/`paraphrase`/`skip`) — KG-native moves wrap the store mutation + the `_kg_snapshot` re-read in `KG_DEGRADED_ERRORS` and re-raise as `KGUnavailableError` → the new `kg_unavailable` 503 handler ("your session is unaffected; try again shortly"); `get_trace` is Postgres-only, unaffected. **authored-set provisioning** — Neo4j-native with no meaningful degraded path (teacher-facing), so every `get_neo4j_client()` call routes through a local `_require_neo` guard → the same 503. `KGStore.__init__` now accepts `neo: Neo4jClient | None`; every Neo4j-backed method (`write_nodes`/`write_edges`/`read_graph`/`read_node_created_at`/`read_node_graded_at`/`walk_chain`/`delete_subgraph`/`stamp_graded_at`/the three negotiation moves via `_set_node_status_neo4j`) calls a `self._require_neo(stage=...)` guard at entry, raising `KGUnavailableError` when `neo is None`; Postgres-only methods (`freeze`/`unfreeze`/`get_node_trace`/the session-lookup helpers) are unaffected. `get_neo4j_client()` in `api.py` never raises — a construction failure logs and returns `None`, with NO NEGATIVE CACHING (the singleton is retried fresh on the next request). When Neo4j is healthy, every route/handler is BYTE-IDENTICAL to before this change.
- **§8B auto-provisioning fail-CLOSED convention (WU-3B2e)**: the §8B solution-lifecycle gates INVERT the §6 runtime fail-open default. The §6 `leakage_judge` (and the soft-failing triviality/intent/summarizer helpers above) prefer a false-NEGATIVE on a parse glitch — they let content THROUGH so a transient JSON error never blocks a legitimate Apollo reply (`leakage_judge.py:126-129` returns `leaks=False, confidence=0.0`). The §8B `find_or_generate`/`validate_pair` (`apollo/provisioning/solution.py`/`pairing_gate.py`) do the OPPOSITE: auto-provisioning prefers a false-REJECT to a false-APPROVE, because an approved pair becomes TEACHABLE for every student. So an unparseable/empty/Problem-invalid generate raises `SolutionDraftError`, and an unparseable/non-object/exception judge response — at EITHER phase — yields `PairingVerdict(paired=False, faithful=False, confidence=0.0)` (a REJECT). All `judge_fn` calls route through one `_judge_or_fail_closed` helper so the fail-closed default lives in a single place; reverting it to fail-open is the pinned mutation `test_validate_pair_fails_closed_on_*` red-discriminates. **§1.8/OPS-6 residual caveat**: the pairing gate REDUCES but does NOT eliminate the fabricated-coherent-WRONG case — a solution that is internally coherent but factually wrong can still pass Phase A + Phase B + all 8 promotion gates and IS then shown to students in SHADOW (a diagnostic with NO Layer-3 belief movement, since `APOLLO_GRAPH_SIM_LAYER3_ENABLED` is OFF). The real pre-exposure safety is therefore the `APOLLO_AUTOPROVISION_ENABLED` flag-OFF default + the §6.7 calibration gate; the retroactive catch is 3B2h quarantine. 3B2e must not claim to prevent this case. The unit writes NO row and reads NO learner state (inputs are COURSE MATERIAL only); its `pairing_verdict` log line carries counts + booleans + `solution_source` ONLY — no solution/question/passage text, no PII.
- **GEN-1 generated-problem statement leak guard (`provisioning/problem_leak_guard.py`)**: standalone `check_problem_leak(problem, *, chat_fn=None) -> ProblemLeakVerdict` for the future GEN-2 write gate (not wired into a pipeline yet). Layer 1 extracts explicit target assignments and final-step numeric/symbolic results, tolerantly matches equivalent numeric spellings/rounding in `problem_text`, and always excludes `given_values`; prose with no extractable answer abstains safely. Layer 2 runs only on that abstention when a caller injects a `MeteredChat.cheap`-shaped callable, requests strict `json_schema` at temperature 0.0, and acts on `leaked=true` only at confidence ≥ 0.6; low-confidence positives and judge failures are advisory clean verdicts because generated rows are held for teacher review. The structured handoff is `{leaked, confidence, reasons, method=deterministic|judge}`. Calc/Bernoulli and MGMT-style qualitative fixtures pin deterministic precision, prose abstention, metered-call shape, and confidence gating.
- **Subject-AGNOSTIC provisioning — CONTENT-DERIVED gate applicability (the spine; supersedes the subject-profile approach, design `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-26-subject-agnostic-promotion-gates-design.md`)**: there is ONE pipeline, no subject detection, no stored profile, no per-epistemology validator registry. Validity is checked against the problem's OWN authored content (spec §3). `subject_profile.py` and the `apollo_subjects` profile columns / migration are GONE. The active-gate set is computed by the CALLER from the problem's content via `promotion_lint.content_active_gates(graph) -> frozenset[int]`: the **structural core {1, 2, 3, 5, 8}** ALWAYS applies; the **symbolic rigor gates {4, 6, 7}** self-activate ONLY when the graph carries a parseable equation (`_has_parseable_equation`). A rigor gate can only ever ADD a rejection to content it applies to — it physically cannot block a subject it does not apply to (spec §4 the additive-oracle safety property). `run_promotion_lint(..., active_gates=...)` keeps the seam (defaults to `ALL_PROMOTION_GATES` for back-compat); gate 1 ALWAYS runs (it builds the `Problem`+`KGGraph`), and the active set is passed IN so the lint stays PURE / DB-free / LLM-free. **Gate 5 is a kind-agnostic GRAPH PROPERTY (spec §4.1):** the structural head + chain-coverage half (unique terminal sink) always runs; the symbolic half self-activates on a parseable terminal equation and checks it computes the single GRAPH-DERIVED answer (`_derive_symbolic_answer` = all equation free symbols − givens − coupling intermediates − cancelled; a prose `target_unknown` no longer blocks a symbolic system that closes to one unknown). **Gate 4** drops the prose `target_unknown` add and, when NO seeded `canonical_symbols` table exists (a fresh auto-minted concept), grounds each symbol against the problem's OWN closure (givens / definition / variable_mapping / computed intermediate / cancelled / the lone answer — `_internal_grounded_symbols`, SUPERSET-accept; the seeded-table path is byte-identical to today, so the 41 seeded ss=2 `:Canon` never move). **Gate 7 (Option 2)** = the system is closed iff the graph-derived answer is ≤ 1 unknown; `> 1` is under-determined → reject. **`promote`** computes `content_active_gates(annotated)`, runs the lint with it, and stamps `payload["verification"] = "mechanically_verified"` (a symbolic oracle fired and passed) `| "faithfulness_only"` (rode the structural core + the LLM faithfulness judge only — spec §5 honesty handle; a future higher human-review bar). **Asymmetric safety:** every loosening only converts a false-RED → pass for self-grounded content; the symbolic oracle stays a HARD gate wherever equations exist, and gate 7 + faithfulness catch under-determination. Proven by the DIFFERENTIAL anchor test (new content-derived pipeline ≡ old all-8 on the in-repo 41 stand-in) + the 6 AAE 333 fixtures flipping reject → promote (`apollo/provisioning/tests/test_promotion_lint.py`). **Direction-B named tiers (the surface `content_active_gates` is driven by):** `STRUCTURAL_CORE_GATES = {1,2,3,5,8}` (the always-on floor) + `RIGOR_LAYERS` (a list of `(applies?(graph), gate_numbers)` pairs — v1 ships exactly one, the symbolic layer `(_symbolic_layer_applies, {4,6,7})`) + the faithfulness oracle (`pairing_gate`, run by the orchestrator). A rigor layer's gates enter the active set ONLY when its `applies?` holds, so a missing/inapplicable mechanical oracle physically cannot block a subject — the next oracle (units-checking, code-execution) is a new layer with no structural-core edit. **Schema (`apollo/schemas/problem.py`):** `given_values` / `target_unknown` stay OPTIONAL (default `{}` / `""`) so a prose problem may omit them; a symbolic problem still carries them and the symbolic gates enforce the contract.
- **Subject-AGNOSTIC provisioning — CONTENT-DERIVED gate applicability (the spine; supersedes the subject-profile approach, design `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-26-subject-agnostic-promotion-gates-design.md`)**: there is ONE pipeline, no subject detection, no stored profile, no per-epistemology validator registry. Validity is checked against the problem's OWN authored content (spec §3). `subject_profile.py` and the `apollo_subjects` profile columns / migration are GONE. The active-gate set is computed by the CALLER from the problem's content via `promotion_lint.content_active_gates(graph) -> frozenset[int]`: the **structural core {1, 2, 3, 5, 8}** ALWAYS applies; the **symbolic rigor gates {4, 6, 7}** self-activate ONLY when the graph carries a parseable equation (`_has_parseable_equation`); the separate **solve/check gate {9}** activates only when content contains both a parseable governing system and a target-isolating stated answer. A rigor gate can only ever ADD a rejection to content it applies to — it physically cannot block a subject it does not apply to (spec §4 the additive-oracle safety property). `run_promotion_lint(..., active_gates=...)` keeps the seam (defaults to `ALL_PROMOTION_GATES` for back-compat); gate 1 ALWAYS runs (it builds the `Problem`+`KGGraph`), and the active set is passed IN so the lint stays PURE / DB-free / LLM-free. **Gate 5 is a kind-agnostic GRAPH PROPERTY (spec §4.1):** the structural head + chain-coverage half (unique terminal sink) always runs; the symbolic half self-activates on a parseable terminal equation and checks it computes the single GRAPH-DERIVED answer (`_derive_symbolic_answer` = all equation free symbols − givens − coupling intermediates − cancelled; a prose `target_unknown` no longer blocks a symbolic system that closes to one unknown). **Gate 4** drops the prose `target_unknown` add and, when NO seeded `canonical_symbols` table exists (a fresh auto-minted concept), grounds each symbol against the problem's OWN closure (givens / definition / variable_mapping / computed intermediate / cancelled / the lone answer — `_internal_grounded_symbols`, SUPERSET-accept; the seeded-table path is byte-identical to today, so the 41 seeded ss=2 `:Canon` never move). **Gate 7 (Option 2)** remains the paper-count closure check: the system is closed iff the graph-derived answer is ≤ 1 unknown after declared bound and assumption-bearing parameters join the existing given/cancelled knowns; `> 1` is under-determined → reject. **Gate 9 (solve/check)** is a distinct pure rigor layer: each SymPy solve runs in a killable child process with a hard timeout; target solutions are compared to the separately stated answer by residual simplification, then deterministic pole/domain-avoiding numeric sampling. Its typed verdicts are `verified` (pass), `refuted` (fail with solved-vs-stated diagnostic), and `unresolved` (non-pass); authored-set orchestration persists unresolved as `held_for_review`, while generic/legacy promotion callers still fail closed. **`promote`** computes `content_active_gates(annotated)`, runs the lint with it, and stamps `payload["verification"] = "mechanically_verified"` (a symbolic oracle fired and passed) `| "faithfulness_only"` (rode the structural core + the LLM faithfulness judge only — spec §5 honesty handle; a future higher human-review bar). **Asymmetric safety:** every loosening only converts a false-RED → pass for self-grounded content; the symbolic oracle stays a HARD gate wherever equations exist, and gate 7 + faithfulness catch under-determination. Proven by the DIFFERENTIAL anchor test (new content-derived pipeline ≡ old all-8 on the in-repo 41 stand-in) + the 6 AAE 333 fixtures flipping reject → promote (`apollo/provisioning/tests/test_promotion_lint.py`). **Direction-B named tiers (the surface `content_active_gates` is driven by):** `STRUCTURAL_CORE_GATES = {1,2,3,5,8}` (the always-on floor) + `RIGOR_LAYERS` (a list of `(applies?(graph), gate_numbers)` pairs — the symbolic layer `(_symbolic_layer_applies, {4,6,7})` plus the stricter solve/check layer `(_solve_check_layer_applies, {9})`) + the faithfulness oracle (`pairing_gate`, run by the orchestrator). A rigor layer's gates enter the active set ONLY when its `applies?` holds, so a missing/inapplicable mechanical oracle physically cannot block a subject — the next oracle (units-checking, code-execution) is a new layer with no structural-core edit. **Schema (`apollo/schemas/problem.py`):** `given_values` / `target_unknown` stay OPTIONAL (default `{}` / `""`) so a prose problem may omit them; a symbolic problem still carries them and the symbolic gates enforce the contract.
- **Authored-problem ingest (`apollo/provisioning/ingest.py`) — Stage-1, REPLACES scrape**: textbook scraping is removed from scope (design spec §1); the Stage-1 entry now ingests a STRUCTURED professor-authored problem set (one problem per record, every field explicit — never re-introducing extraction loss). Each record → an `AuthoredProblem` (statement + optional solution + optional worked_procedure), classified by `classify_completeness` into **worked** / **answer_only** / **none** (Stage-5 builds the reference graph differently per case). `write_authored_tier1_problems` mirrors `scrape.write_tier1_problems` (tier=1 EXPLICIT, content-derived `authored.<statement_hash>` `problem_code`, SELECT-then-skip idempotency, denormalized `search_space_id`) but stamps `solution_source='authored'` and carries the authored ground truth (solution + procedure + completeness) in the payload so Stage-5 grounds faithfulness on the professor's solution, not RAG. `ingest_authored_problems` writes the Tier-1 inventory and **commits INDEPENDENTLY** (`commit=True`) — the load-bearing fix for the write-then-rollback hazard (the legacy orchestrator committed once at run end, so an interrupted run lost all ingested inventory; now the inventory is durable the instant ingest returns, regardless of downstream). No subject profile is detected or persisted — gate applicability is content-derived at promote time (`subject_id` is retained only for course scoping). Fail-soft per record (a record with no statement is dropped + counted, never a run abort); NO LLM / NO network in this unit.
- **Authored reference-graph construction + per-candidate pipeline (Stage-5, SUBJECT-AGNOSTIC)**: `solution.construct_authored_reference(authored, *, chat_fn)` STRUCTURES the professor's solution into a typed reference graph over the UNIVERSAL mint-map vocab (the 6 `_ENTRY_TYPE_TO_KIND_PREFIX` entry types — no per-subject `node_vocab`, no `profile` param), branching on completeness — **worked** = structure the authored procedure, **answer_only** = reconstruct to the known answer, **none** = generate + FLAG `provenance.flagged=True` for review. It NEVER forces a target shape (the construction-side twin of the promotion bug: the old default forced a symbolic target on prose authors), FAIL-CLOSES (`SolutionDraftError`) on an unparseable construction / a node type outside the universal mint map / a non-`Problem`-valid graph, and sets the draft's `grounding` to the AUTHORED solution so the Stage-3 faithfulness judge entails against the professor's ground truth (not RAG'd chunks). `solution_source` ∈ {extracted, generated, **authored**}; `provenance` carries `completeness`/`flagged` only (no `profile_kind` stamp). The faithfulness gate (`pairing_gate.validate_pair`) is UNCHANGED (byte-identical) — it already grounds on `draft.grounding`. `orchestrator.provision_authored_problem` wires the per-candidate pipeline (construct → faithfulness → `tag_and_mint` → CONTENT-gated `promote`) reusing every frozen stage; `promote` derives the applicable gates from the problem's OWN content, so a polisci argument (no parseable equation → symbolic gates self-deactivate) promotes while a fluid problem (carries equations) still runs all 8. A per-candidate failure (un-constructable / unfaithful / lint-rejected) is a CLEAN reject (`AuthoredProvisionResult`), never a run abort (AC #3). The textbook-scrape `run_provisioning` stays intact (back-compat). `tag_and_mint` mints `definition`/`condition`/`procedure_step` via the same mint map.
- **Subject-agnostic teach-back (Goal C, VERIFIED — no new grading code)**: the FROZEN `graph_compare.grade_attempt` (structural coverage/soundness/bisimilarity over typed nodes) and the `learner_model.persist_learner_update` belief write run UNCHANGED on argument graphs — `definition`/`condition`/`procedure_step` are already first-class node types, and the learner model keys on `KGEntity` (kinds `definition`/`procedure`/`condition` are in `ENTITY_KINDS`), so a polisci teach-back grades + updates `apollo_learner_state`/`apollo_mastery_events` through the SAME path as a fluid one (no subject-specific branch). Proof: `apollo/grading/tests/test_subject_fluid_teachback.py` (full + partial argument-graph grades; learner-state + mastery-event writes for an equation, a procedure, and a definition entity).
