The dormant rubric (`compute_rubric`) + opposes/contradiction machinery remain available for counterargument/misconception grading (deferred).
- **`variable_mapping` contract — mint-map ↔ node-type-map symmetry (G4, 2026-07-02)**: `variable_mapping` is a real ontology `NodeType` (`nodes.py`, `VariableMappingContent{term, symbol}`), the schema `EntryType` accepts it, and the WU-AAS authored-construction vocab + mint map (`persistence.learner_model_seed._ENTRY_TYPE_TO_KIND_PREFIX`, `varmap.*`) EMIT it wherever the LLM structures a symbol↔term binding — a minted `ConceptProblem.payload` therefore reaches the graph-sim chain carrying `variable_mapping` reference steps. The resolver/canonical node-type map (`resolution.candidates._ENTRY_TYPE_TO_NODE_TYPE`, imported by `graph_compare.canonical`) originally OMITTED it, so `candidates_from_reference_solution` / `build_reference_canonical` raised `KeyError: 'variable_mapping'` on every minted problem carrying one (the F1c `linear_motion` crash — the seeded subjects never use `variable_mapping`, so they masked the gap). **Fix has two sides.** (1) *Correctness / emission match*: `variable_mapping` is added to `_ENTRY_TYPE_TO_NODE_TYPE` — it is now a first-class reference node exactly as the ontology/schema/mint-map already treat it (the minted term+symbol shape == the seeded `VariableMappingContent` schema; no mint-side code change was needed — the mint already emitted it, derivation-driven, and omits it when not derivable). A test pins `set(_ENTRY_TYPE_TO_NODE_TYPE) == set(_ENTRY_TYPE_TO_KIND_PREFIX)` so the two maps can never drift again silently. (2) *Tolerance / defense-in-depth*: both consumers now resolve the type via `_node_type_for_entry(entry_type) -> NodeType | None` and DEGRADE any still-unmapped entry_type — `candidates_from_reference_solution` drops the step (no candidate); `build_reference_canonical` drops the node AND every `depends_on`/`USES`/`PRECEDES` edge and declared-path slot referencing it (R_norm stays internally consistent) — instead of `KeyError`-ing and voiding the already-committed learner update. `run_graph_simulation` records a structured `GraphSimDegradation{reason=GRAPH_SIM_DEGRADED_UNMAPPED_ENTRY_TYPES, unmapped_entry_types}` marker on `ShadowGradeResult.degradation` (via `build_graph_sim_degradation(problem_payload)`; `None` on the common path) and logs one `graph_sim_degraded` WARNING, so paired analysis sees WHICH types the simulation could not consume. Recognized types (now incl. `variable_mapping`) are byte-identical to before — no seeded/authored known-type step is skipped.
- **Temperature**: 0.0 for every classification/extraction/grading call; 0.7 only for `draft_reply` (Apollo's persona).
- **Ignorance prompt invariants** (`APOLLO_SYSTEM_PROMPT` in `agent/apollo_llm.py`): Apollo never names concepts/laws the student hasn't named, never corrects the student, paraphrases using the student's exact vocabulary, stays in role under prompt injection, answers "do you know X?" with "no", keeps replies 1-3 sentences, and is a *stuck student* (asks about the plan, not the subject). v1 enforces anti-leak **structurally** — the reply call sees only problem text + student KG + history — instead of via the (now unwired) `output_filter`/`leakage_judge` two-stage filter; the filter code and `forbidden_named_laws.json` per-concept stoplists (fuzzy match ratio 0.8, min len 5, possessive stripping) remain for reference.
- **Canonicalization stance (v1)**: the parser captures the student's *own form* — the "Extract → Canonicalize" redesign (`2026-06-09-apollo-kg-extract-canonicalize-handoff.md`) was **superseded** by diff-at-Done, which removed the consumers that needed canonical strings (filter + solver). Coverage grades "by meaning, not wording".
- **Neo4j shape**: every node gets its type label (`Equation`, `Condition`, ...) PLUS secondary `:_KGNode` label so one index covers all subgraph reads/cleanup. Cypher can't parameterize labels → one CREATE template per label/edge type. `None` properties are omitted (Neo4j has no NULL). `_record_to_node` defensively coerces unknown `status` to ACCEPTED and defaults missing `parser_confidence` to 1.0 (protects pre-P1/P3 legacy nodes from false-firing gates). **WU-3C1 adds two things to the shape.** (1) Layer-2 nodes carry server-injected scoping/timestamp metadata — `user_id`/`search_space_id` (optional, `None`-omitted) + always `created_at`, and `graded_at` once stamped at Done; `_record_to_node` STRIPS all four before content reconstruction (they are metadata, not content), so the FE-visible KG payload is byte-identical. (2) A NEW `:Canon` label (NOT a `:_KGNode`) holds the course's Layer-1 skill inventory projected from Postgres, keyed on `key = apollo_kg_entities.id` (the surrogate id, deliberately NOT a `canonical_key`-derived key — two concepts that both mint the same `canonical_key` must stay TWO distinct `:Canon` nodes or every future `RESOLVES_TO` edge cross-contaminates). `:Canon` is rebuildable from Postgres (`canon_projection.project_canon`), never authored in Neo4j. **WU-3C2 adds the resolution shape.** Each `:_KGNode` gains four server-side resolution node-fields once the §5 resolver has run — `resolution` (`resolved`/`unresolved`/`ambiguous`), `resolved_key`, `resolution_method`, `resolution_confidence` — written by `resolution_store.persist_resolution_fields`; `_record_to_node` STRIPS all four on read (metadata, not content) so the FE-visible KG payload stays byte-identical (`resolved_key` is `None`-omitted when unresolved). And a NEW `(:_KGNode)-[:RESOLVES_TO {method, confidence, resolved_at}]->(:Canon)` CROSS-LABEL edge links each resolved student node to its canonical target (idempotent `MERGE` on the endpoint pair). `RESOLVES_TO` is written by `resolution_store`'s own Cypher and is intentionally NOT in `EdgeType`/`EDGE_ALLOWED_PAIRS` (those govern within-subgraph `:_KGNode→:_KGNode` edges).
- **NLI tier — grading-time injection and chat-path threading (LIVE, default ON as of 2026-07-01):** By default (NLI is now DEFAULT-ON; `APOLLO_NLI_ENABLED=0` is the kill switch), `handlers/done_grading.py::_nli_context()` returns a populated `NLIContext` backed by a process-singleton `TransformersNLIAdjudicator` (lazy-init, CPU device, model = `active_nli_model()` — `APOLLO_NLI_MODEL` env, default the tuned `cross-encoder/nli-deberta-v3-large`); the singleton is held in module-level `_NLI_ADJUDICATOR` and re-used across Done calls to avoid repeated model loads. **Grading-path budget cap + threading (2026-07-01 fix):** mirroring the chat-path cap, `run_graph_simulation` caps grading-path NLI usage by student-node count via `APOLLO_NLI_GRADING_MAX_NODES` (default 15; campaign/probe runs opt into 40 via the env override — 2026-07-05 routing Fix 1, revised opt-in shape) — an attempt whose `student_graph` exceeds the cap grades WITHOUT NLI (`nli_ctx` forced to `None`, logged `nli_grading_skipped_budget`) rather than aborting. When the NLI tier is active, the grading-path `resolve_attempt` call is now offloaded to a worker thread via `asyncio.to_thread` (`done_grading._resolve_attempt_async`), mirroring the chat path's `run_in_executor` offload, so CPU-bound transformer inference no longer blocks the FastAPI event loop during Done; when NLI is inactive the call stays inline (byte-identical to pre-offload). **Graceful missing-`transformers` degrade (2026-07-01 fix):** if the `transformers` package is missing at either `NLIContext` construction (`_nli_context`) or during the offloaded `resolve_attempt` call, grading now logs `apollo_nli_transformers_unavailable` ONCE per process and proceeds WITHOUT NLI, rather than setting `learner_update_pending=True` and re-raising forever (the pre-fix behavior was a permanent retry-loop failure). Prod boot does not pre-warm by default — the model is still loaded lazily on the first real inference call there. An opt-in boot-time pre-warm hook exists for the local campaign harness (2026-07-02): `server.py`'s `_prewarm_nli_on_startup()` FastAPI startup handler checks `APOLLO_NLI_PREWARM` (default OFF, truthy `1`/`true`/`yes`) and, when set, calls `apollo.resolution.nli_adjudicator.prewarm()` — constructs a throwaway `TransformersNLIAdjudicator` for `active_nli_model()` and runs one dummy `classify("a","a")`, forcing the checkpoint to load (downloading into `HF_HOME` if not already cached) before any request arrives. `prewarm()` does NOT populate `done_grading`'s process-lived `_NLI_ADJUDICATOR` singleton — the guarantee it provides is that the checkpoint files land on local disk under `HF_HOME`, so the grading path's own lazy singleton construction reads from disk instead of the network on ITS first real call. A prewarm failure is caught and logged (`apollo_nli_prewarm_failed`) and never blocks server boot. `campaign/infra/prewarm_nli.py` (`python -m campaign.infra.prewarm_nli`) is the standalone CLI used to seed/verify the `HF_HOME` cache ahead of a campaign run; it prints separate `load_seconds` / `first_classify_seconds` timings (verified 2026-07-02: cold run against an empty `HF_HOME` ≈ 89s including the HF download of `cross-encoder/nli-deberta-v3-large`; a second run against the SAME `HF_HOME` with `HF_HUB_OFFLINE=1` — network calls disallowed — loaded in ≈ 4.5s, confirming the "no first-request HF download" contract, spec §5). On the chat path (`handlers/chat.py`), `run_clarification_detection` receives the same `NLIContext` but is budget-gated: when the turn's parsed-node count exceeds `APOLLO_NLI_CHAT_MAX_NODES` (default 15), `_nli_ctx` is set to `None` for that turn and the call degrades gracefully to lexical-only (logged `nli_chat_skipped_budget`). When NLI is active, `find_residual_nodes` is dispatched via `asyncio.get_running_loop().run_in_executor(None, …)` so the CPU-bound model never blocks the async event loop; on the flag-off path the call is synchronous (byte-identical to pre-NLI code, no executor overhead). Fail-safe throughout: any NLI failure returns `[]` so teaching never blocks. Although the tier is now default-ON in production, the TEST SUITE still forces it OFF so the real model is never loaded in CI — TWO autouse `_force_nli_off` guards set `APOLLO_NLI_ENABLED=0`: `apollo/conftest.py` (unit suite) AND `tests/conftest.py` (the `tests/database/` integration suite that drives the real `handle_done` path). Opt-in NLI tests re-enable via their own `monkeypatch.setenv("APOLLO_NLI_ENABLED", "1")` (a function-scoped monkeypatch wins over the autouse guard).
- **Confidence thresholds form a ladder**: cheap-LLM judges act at ≥ 0.6 (triviality, leakage); intent confirmation gate at ≥ 0.7; OLM clarification invite at parse-confidence < 0.7; Done-gate (final brake) at < 0.6; coverage binary matches with confidence < 0.5 are downgraded to "missing" and logged `coverage_uncertain`.
- **Abstention gate — status & the recall/denominator distinction (VERIFIED against live `abstention.py` 2026-07-06; recorded here so the superseded "resolver recall is the bottleneck" framing does not recur):** `apply_abstention` sets `abstained` via TWO independent triggers — `unresolved_rate > 0.35` and, since Phase 1c, `normalization_confidence < 0.85`. **The normalization trigger is the one that was FIXED** (MVP recalibration, `docs/_archive/handoffs/2026-06-26-apollo-grader-mvp-fix-handoff.md`): on the econ re-run, abstention dropped **15/15 → 7/15** and the normalization trigger stopped firing entirely (**10/15 → 0**); it is keyed on resolution *quality* (weakest-link nc) and correctly sits ABOVE the `derived@0.95`/`alias@0.92` tiers. **The `unresolved_rate` trigger is the one still OPEN, and it is NOT a resolver-recall failure.** Its denominator is `len(resolution.resolved)` — the count of ALL parsed student nodes (`unresolved_rate_of`), NOT the reference set. A student asserts far more than the reference set (measured mean **16.3** parsed nodes, range 5–34, vs reference sets mean **4.4**, range 2–7), so even a fully-covered attempt lands near 0.50 > 0.35 and abstains. Full-corpus verification of all 31 gradeable F1c attempts (`docs/_archive/handoffs/2026-07-06-weekend-worker-a-handoff.md`) measured **reference-node recall at 100%** — every reference node a persona taught correctly WAS credited, zero genuine resolver misses — so the residual abstention is a **volume-denominator / threshold-discrimination artifact, not low recall.** The June-26 node-recovery framing ("~38% unresolved / recall is the upstream bottleneck", `docs/_archive/experiments/2026-06-26-apollo-grader-node-recovery-e2e/FEEDBACK.md`) is **SUPERSEDED** by this measurement. The `APOLLO_ABSTENTION_COMPOSITE` gate (default OFF, `COMPOSITE_DEFAULT_COVERAGE_MIN = 0.6`) is the proposed reference-anchored CONTENT-signal replacement (`node_coverage ≥ coverage_min`) for the volume denominator; it stays OFF because the terminal weekend finding was that no single `unresolved_rate` floor separates strong/partial attempts from misconception/vague controls (rates interleave across ~0.35–0.92; by a 0.45 floor a control already grades — and would grade WRONG) — a metric-redesign problem, not a threshold tweak. None of the three weekend iterations were promoted.
- **Negotiable OLM (P3)**: moves mutate the Neo4j node (`status`, `student_belief`) AND append an immutable audit row to `apollo_kg_negotiations`; the Done-gate clears once each flagged entry has ≥ 1 move. DUAL + `student_belief` redirects coverage to grade the student's wording (for procedure steps it *replaces* `action`).
- **Freeze discipline**: writes/moves check phase via Postgres before touching Neo4j; reads are allowed while frozen.
- **Retention (§7, WU-3C1)**: `handle_end` now PERSISTS per-attempt subgraphs (it no longer deletes — it only marks the session `ended` in Postgres); `done.py` stamps `graded_at` on the frozen graph as the final, idempotent, post-commit retention write (Δt-anchoring in Layer-3 reads the stored value, never `now()`); `restart_problem` is the ONE explicit student wipe that still calls `delete_subgraph`; `delete_subgraph` remains in `KGStore` as the future janitor's pruning primitive; the `attempt_id < 0` test-cleanup convention is unchanged.
- **`summarize_for_apollo` format is contract**: the bullet shapes (`- equation (label): symbolic`, `- variable: term → symbol`, procedure steps ordered via the PRECEDES chain) are Apollo's vocabulary mirror — see `apollo/agent/LEAKAGE_POLICY.md`; don't change casually.
- **§8A curriculum cutover (WU-3D) — landed**: the curriculum is now fully DB-resolved and course-scoped. The hard-coded `_AVAILABLE_CLUSTERS` constant, the `_CLUSTER_TO_CONCEPT` map / `cluster_to_concept` / `list_problems_for_cluster` functions, and `infer_concept_cluster` are DELETED; the runtime resolves candidate concepts from `apollo_concepts WHERE …search_space_id`, picks problems from `apollo_concept_problems` by `concept_id`, and populates `apollo_sessions.concept_id`. Migration 027 dropped the legacy `apollo_sessions.concept_cluster_id` column (ORM column dropped in lockstep). `sympy_exec._CANONICAL_SYMBOLS` is still a fluid-mechanics list (out of WU-3D scope). `apollo_sessions.student_id` was dropped in migration 023 (replaced by `user_id UUID` referencing `auth.users`).
- **Tests**: nearly all `*/tests/` modules are `pytest.mark.skip`-ed with "Tracked in claude_v3_checklist.md item 1; will be re-enabled in test-rewrite phase". Live Neo4j tests use negative attempt_ids (cleanup contract in `apollo/conftest.py`). The LIVE (non-skipped) parser test modules are `test_triviality.py`, `test_parser_confidence.py`, `test_prompt_builder.py`, `test_typed_edge_extraction.py` (WU-2A + WU-2B nit-1), `test_graph_context_builder.py`, `test_edge_resolver_precedence.py`, and `test_parser_imports.py` (WU-2B) — the GPT-4o call is mocked via `@patch("apollo.parser.parser_llm.OpenAI")`, no Neo4j / no network. The LIVE store tests `test_store_negotiation.py`, `test_store_write_edges.py`, and `test_store_write_nodes_dedup.py` (WU-2B) use a fake async Neo4j session (no live driver); the chat wiring test `test_chat_crossturn.py` (WU-2B) mocks `parse_utterance`/`draft_reply`/`KGStore` (no Neo4j / no LLM). **WU-3C2 resolver + persistence tests** are all LIVE: `apollo/resolution/tests/` (errors, candidates, result, tiers, structural, competition, assignment, resolver — resolution is now pure content-tiers + clarification; `adjudication.py` and the `llm_adjudicator` param were removed in Task 4; `llm_calls == 0` always; no live OpenAI call ever fires) is PURE-UNIT and the symbolic tier exercises real SymPy + RapidFuzz; `apollo/knowledge_graph/tests/test_resolution_store_mapping.py` pins the DB-free spec/Cypher seams with fake clients; the real-Neo4j modules `apollo/knowledge_graph/tests/test_resolution_store_neo4j.py` (RESOLVES_TO write, field round-trip, idempotent re-resolution, the folded WU-3C1 scoping-prop persist-and-strip nit) and `tests/database/test_resolution_resolves_to_postgres.py` (the full WU-3B→3C1→3C2 chain: seed Postgres entities → `project_canon` → resolve → `write_resolution` lands `RESOLVES_TO` on the right `:Canon` key) use the LOCAL `tc_neo4j` / `neo4j_client` + `db_session` Testcontainers fixtures — NEVER Aura, never remote Supabase. **WU-4A1 graph-compare tests** are LIVE and almost entirely PURE-UNIT (`apollo/graph_compare/tests/`: canonical-type immutability, validator gates, R_norm/S_norm builders, problem-inputs assembly) over hand-built `KGGraph` + hand-built `ResolutionResult` + problem dicts — no DB, no LLM, no network; the merge/drop/multi-path branches each have a dedicated test. The ONE test that runs `resolve_attempt` (`test_symbolic_mappings_plumbed_makes_circular_area_resolvable`) passes `llm_adjudicator=None` and resolves on the symbolic tier alone (`llm_calls == 0`, no live call). The SINGLE real-PG graph-compare test is `tests/database/test_graph_compare_symbolic_mappings_roundtrip.py` (`@pytest.mark.integration`, reuses the WU-3B seed harness on a LOCAL Docker pgvector container) — it proves the additive `symbolic_mappings` key survives both seeders into `apollo_concept_problems.payload` with zero seeder code change.
- **Parser edge-rejection (WU-2A) + store edge-rejection (WU-2B)**: `edge_resolver.resolve_typed_edges` rejects an invalid LLM edge by **logging** `parser_edge_rejected` with a `reason` (`unresolvable_ref` / `unknown_endpoint_type` / `self_loop` / `bad_edge_type` / `disallowed_pair` / `validator_rejected` / `malformed_edge`) and dropping it — never silently, never raising, never losing the valid nodes/edges. WU-2B adds the symmetric store-boundary check: `store.write_edges` validates endpoint existence + EDGE_ALLOWED_PAIRS BEFORE the CREATE and logs `write_edge_rejected reason=<endpoint_absent|unknown_endpoint_type|disallowed_pair>` plus a `write_edges attempt_id=… written=… dropped=… invalid=…` summary, returning a `WriteEdgesResult` (no silent drop, no raise — rejections are data). `chat.py` now builds a `GraphContext` from the live attempt graph and threads it into the parser (cross-turn linking live), and `write_nodes` de-dups cross-turn re-assertions by id (`write_nodes … created=… reused=…`).
- **FLAT entry shape (WU-2A)**: the strict `json_schema` makes each `entries[]` item a FLAT object — every node field (`symbolic`/`label`/`variables`/`applies_when`/`transformation`/`concept`/`meaning`/`term`/`symbol`/`action`/`purpose`) plus `confidence`/`reuse_of`/`uses_equation_ordinals` sits directly on the entry (present-and-nullable, never a nested `content`). OpenAI strict mode (`additionalProperties: false`) forbids a `content` key, so the prompt template and `extraction_schema.build_extraction_schema()` both emit the flat field list. `parser_llm._flat_content` lifts the type-specific fields into the nested `content` dict that the ontology's `build_node` expects (the adapter is keyed on `NODE_CONTENT_TYPES.model_fields`, one source of truth). `uses_equation_ordinals` is a nullable int-array on the entry so the deterministic within-turn USES fallback can still fire under the strict schema.
- **Layer-3 belief math (WU-5A1, `apollo/learner_model/`)** — three pins that are easy to get wrong: (1) **Cold-start mastery is 0.50, not 0.40.** The mastery FORMULA `0.5·p_shaky + p_mastered` is authoritative and yields `0.5·0.60 + 0.20 = 0.50` for the cold-start belief `(0.20,0.60,0.20)`; the spec §3 prose that read "0.40" was an arithmetic error, corrected in `2026-06-10-apollo-kg-learner-model-architecture-decision.md` §3 (orchestrator-confirmed 2026-06-18). The belief vector itself is unchanged. (2) **`LIKELIHOOD_FLOOR=0.02` (BKT boundary floor, clamp-EACH-component) is load-bearing, not cosmetic.** It clamps every covered-likelihood component to `≥0.02` before the damper so the perfect-covered extremes `s∈{0,1}` (`(1,0,0)`/`(0,0,1)`) can never zero out `p_misc`/`p_mastered` — without it a single perfect explanation absorbing-zeros a state forever and a later misconception could never re-raise `p_misc`. (3) **The misconception flag is TWO-STEP.** `misconception_code_of` surfaces the code only once `p_misc` is the argmax AND `≥0.5` — a single misconception from cold-start reaches `p_misc≈0.4839` (argmax but UNFLAGGED, returns `None`); the SECOND reaches `p_misc≈0.7475` (flagged). Also: `q = parser_confidence·grader_confidence` ONLY — `event.confidence` (resolution confidence) is NOT folded into `q` (the COVERED score is already resolution-scaled by the §6.5 converter); `dt_days_since_last` is recorded but NO decay is applied in v1 (decay is WU-5B). γ=1.5 (`s=0.5`→shaky, `s=0.25`→misc).
- **The emergent misconception map (2026-07-10 design, `docs/_archive/specs/2026-07-10-emergent-misconception-map-design.md`; increment 2 over the `apollo/emergent/` store) — the capture → accrete → promote → dock loop.** A judge trips at a reference node it can't name (`detector_unkeyed`) or a clarification rescore confirms a misconception (`clarification_refuted`) → an observation is written to the existing `apollo_misconception_observations` ledger → trust accrues across distinct students (`trust = min(1, students/K)·mean_confidence·recency`, `apollo/emergent/config.py`) → at τ_project (0.2) it materializes as a `:Canon` misconception entity (visible on the map, not yet grading) → at τ_assert (0.5) it becomes a live detector candidate that F-struct docks future students against. **The two capture seams**, both wired into `handle_done` (`apollo/handlers/done.py`) gated on `emergent_map_capture_enabled()`: `detector_unkeyed` calls `apollo/overseer/misconception_detector/gate.py::collect_unkeyed_births`, which replays the gate's own row7/row8 unkeyed predicate (pure, no IO) over `detection.per_concept` + `opposes_index`; `clarification_refuted` is captured in `apollo/clarification/resolve_turn.py` on a `RescoreOutcome == "refuted"`. A `sympy_veto` anchor takes precedence over the judge for the SAME `concept_key` — a node already resolved by a sympy-veto finding is excluded from unkeyed collection (fix, commit `a041e1b`). **Signature scheme (D2):** `emergent.<entity_key>` — node-anchored, never re-keyed to `misc.*`; `apollo/graph_compare/soundness.py::is_misconception_key` now accepts BOTH the `misc.` prefix (hand-authored) and the `emergent.` prefix (`EMERGENT_MISCONCEPTION_KEY_PREFIX`, promoted emergent) as contradiction-detection keys, because the emergent signature IS the entity's real `apollo_kg_entities.canonical_key` (remapping it would silently break the lookup). **`entity_key` derivation:** `apollo/persistence/learner_model_seed.py::derive_entity_key`/`_entity_key_for_step` computes `f"{prefix}.{id}"` from `_ENTRY_TYPE_TO_KIND_PREFIX`; `Problem.to_kg_graph` (`apollo/schemas/problem.py`) now derives it at graph-build time when a reference-solution step omits `entity_key` — byte-identical for hand-authored problems (which already carry it), newly populated for provisioned ones. **Two new flags, both independently gated, both default OFF:** `APOLLO_EMERGENT_MAP_CAPTURE` (`emergent_map_capture_enabled()`) gates the two write seams plus eager τ_project materialization — lets staging observe without any grade effect; `APOLLO_EMERGENT_MAP_ASSERT` (`emergent_map_assert_enabled()`) gates the τ_assert grade-feedback read in `apollo/clarification/candidate_assembly.py`. **RUNBOOK NOTE:** the legacy `APOLLO_EMERGENT_MISCONCEPTIONS` flag is UNCHANGED in meaning but its scope NARROWED — it now gates ONLY the increment-1 artifact-derived ledger feed (`record_observations_from_canonical`); the promoted-emergent grade-read it used to also gate MOVED to `APOLLO_EMERGENT_MAP_ASSERT`. Flipping the old flag alone on staging no longer grants grade authority to promoted emergent misconceptions — that requires `APOLLO_EMERGENT_MAP_ASSERT` explicitly. **Eager τ_project materialization:** `apollo/emergent/materialize.py::materialize_if_promotable`, called from BOTH capture seams right after their observation write succeeds, in the SAME failure domain — recomputes trust via the existing `apollo.emergent.store.load_class_misconceptions`, upserts to `apollo_kg_entities kind='misconception'` + an `opposes` link (via `apollo.provisioning.tag_mint_persist`) and projects to `:Canon` (via `apollo.knowledge_graph.canon_projection`); a Neo4j-side projection failure is logged+swallowed (never affects the grade), a Postgres-side failure propagates to the caller's own try/except. **`opposes` is a Postgres PAYLOAD field only** (`apollo_kg_entities.payload.opposes_entity_key`), resolved by string lookup at read time — NOT yet a first-class Neo4j `:Canon` graph edge (follow-up: project `opposes` as a real graph edge). **Prerequisite bug fix (commit `f4df42f`):** `apollo/clarification/candidate_assembly.py`'s `_misconceptions_dict` used to hardcode `"opposes": None` for hand-authored misconceptions, discarding the real `MisconceptionEntry.opposes` column (migration 039); it now threads `e.opposes` through, so authored opposes-links actually reach F-struct's structural matching — a pre-existing defect this branch fixed as a prerequisite for the whole loop to work, not new emergent-map code per se. **Migration 040** (`database/migrations/040_apollo_misconception_obs_source_domain.sql`) adds a CHECK constraint enumerating `apollo_misconception_observations.source` to `('grading_artifact', 'detector_unkeyed', 'clarification_refuted')`. NOT applied to any remote Supabase project — agents apply to LOCAL Docker Postgres only, test rehearsal then prod is a human/CI step.

- **DAG-3 generation hardening (2026-07-12, problem-generation master plan Track 0.4).** (1) The reference-solution generation contract is authored ONCE: `apollo/provisioning/generation_contract.py::ontology_block()` is sourced verbatim by all three generation prompts (`solution.py` extract/generate + augment variant, `authored_sets/graph_derivation.py` derivation, `solution.py` authored construction) — add a step-contract rule THERE, never in a prompt. (2) `find_or_generate` now runs the derivation path's defect-detect→retry harness: `GENERATION_DEFECT_CLASSES` (the vocabulary-independent subset — no `foreign_symbol`, no `node_count`) over the draft, up to `_GENERATION_DEFECT_RETRIES`(=2) feedback retries with the localized defect list + the model's own previous draft echoed back; on exhaustion the draft is FLAGGED (`provenance.generation_defects`) and returned — never crashed — because generated solutions are auto-held for teacher review (PR #127). Schema-invalid drafts still fail closed via `_validate_problem_shape`, unchanged. (3) New defect classes in `find_derivation_defects` (now class-selectable via `classes=`): `dependency_completeness` (an equation using symbol X must reach X's variable_mapping/definition binder through its TRANSITIVE `depends_on`; problem givens / bound variables / target / `symbolic_mappings` keys / `SHARED_CONSTANT_SYMBOLS` are whitelisted so shared constants never fabricate a false dep; condition edges neither provide nor require symbol coverage), `semantic_key` (bans `step_2`/`eq1`-style type/position echoes in ids AND `entity_key` slugs — `GENERIC_ID_TOKENS`), and `symbol_table` (OPTIONAL top-level `symbol_table` {symbol → role/ontology_key/unit}; absent = legacy, no defect; when present it must cover every equation symbol CASE-SENSITIVELY — m and M are two quantities — the mint-time input that kills both fragmentation and false merges; captured into `provenance.symbol_table`). Every symbolic defect class self-deactivates on prose (zero defects, zero retries on qualitative drafts — pinned in `test_generation_hardening.py`).
- **DAG-4 KC-anchored authored-set granularity (2026-07-12, problem-generation master plan Track 3.1).** `authored_sets/graph_derivation.py` selects its derivation prompt per call using the default-OFF `APOLLO_KC_GRANULARITY` flag. OFF preserves the legacy prompt byte-for-byte and its 5–9-node validator bound. ON asks for one node per separately assessable knowledge component (KLI framing), lets the worked solution determine a natural node count within a 3–15 sanity bound, and applies the matching validator bound. This affects newly derived DAGs only; existing seeded and persisted problems are not migrated or re-derived. `scripts/dag4_granularity_eval.py` is the manual live-LLM comparison harness: it runs three calculus and three equationless MGMT fixtures with the flag OFF/ON and reports node counts, derivation defects/retries, and content-selected promotion-lint verdicts side by side.
- **DAG-5 safeguarded contraction grading (2026-07-12, problem-generation master plan Track 3.2).** The default-OFF `APOLLO_GRAPH_CONTRACTION_ENABLED` flag lets the shadow graph comparer recognize up to three omitted `equation`/`simplification` nodes on a contiguous non-branching reference-path segment when the student graph directly bridges covered endpoints. Every eligible intermediate is checked independently with the existing NLI thresholds against the bridge evidence: an entailed, non-contradicted step becomes `covered_by_contraction` and receives covered-style mastery evidence; an unproved or unavailable-model result fails closed to `not_demonstrated`, receives no coverage credit, and emits no missing `s=0.0` mastery event. For concrete equation intermediates, parseable bridge equations now pass through a SymPy equivalence-confirm/same-LHS-veto channel before NLI, preventing symbol-overlap entailment from crediting an algebraically wrong value while retaining NLI fallback for word-only or unparseable evidence. Prose graphs self-deactivate, and flag OFF preserves the prior comparison exactly. `scripts/dag5_contraction_replay.py` is the manual Docker-backed OFF/ON corpus harness reporting coverage, contraction verdicts, and removed missing-event deltas.

## Product context

Apollo implements **learning-by-teaching** (protégé effect): explaining a concept to a naive
agent forces the student to surface their own understanding; the system grades the *teaching*,
not answers to questions. Pedagogical commitments visible in code: Apollo never corrects the
student mid-session (misconceptions are detected silently and graded at Done); the diagnostic
report is formative ("you didn't walk Apollo through X"), never punitive; the Negotiable OLM
(challenge/paraphrase/skip, after Bull & Pain's Mr Collins and STyLE-OLM) lets the student
contest what the parser claims they said before being graded on it; XP/levels (Apollo
Apprentice → Archon) reward completion with reduced credit for re-attempts. Prefer smaller,
higher-leverage v1 shipments over feature-complete ones (project memory:
`feedback_apollo_pedagogy_choices.md`).

Active redesign working docs (read these before any non-trivial Apollo change):
- `ai-ta-backend/docs/apollo-redesign.md` — gap analysis (Gaps A–G) × academic literature map.
- `ai-ta-backend/docs/claude_v3_checklist.md` — itemized V3 flaw checklist; item 1 gates the test rewrite.
- `C:\Users\ultra\OneDrive\TA-test\docs\superpowers\specs\2026-06-09-apollo-diff-at-done-design.md` — the approved v1 design this code currently implements.
- `C:\Users\ultra\OneDrive\TA-test\docs\superpowers\specs\2026-06-09-apollo-kg-extract-canonicalize-handoff.md` — superseded EDC direction (diagnosis still valid).
- `ai-ta-backend/docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-10-apollo-kg-learner-model-architecture-decision.md` §4 (extraction), §5 (edge vocabulary), §6.3 (EDGE_ALLOWED_PAIRS) — the KG learner-model redesign; WU-2A implements the §4 one-call typed-edge extraction with provenance.
- `ai-ta-backend/docs/superpowers/plans/2026-06-15-apollo-kg-wu2a-typed-edge-extraction.md` — WU-2A plan (context-aware one-call typed-edge extraction + explicit/inferred provenance, parser-only).
- `ai-ta-backend/docs/superpowers/plans/2026-06-15-apollo-kg-wu2b-crossturn-writeedges.md` — WU-2B plan (cross-turn linking wired in `chat.py` via `build_graph_context`, `store.write_edges` validate-then-create + structured logging, `store.write_nodes` cross-turn id de-dup, and three inherited WU-2A LOW nits).
